## Module: `ai::behavior_tree` {#ai-behavior-tree}

*Source: `src/ai/behavior_tree.rs`*

Behavior Tree with composite, decorator, and leaf nodes.

All nodes return `BTStatus`. Composites memo the running-child index
to support multi-frame "running" states.

---

### `enum BTStatus`  · [line 15](src/ai/behavior_tree.rs#L15)

Return status produced by every BT node after a tick.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub enum BTStatus
```

**Variants:**

| Variant | Description |
|---------|-------------|
| `Success` | Success variant. |
| `Failure` | Failure variant. |
| `Running` | Running variant. |

## Module: `ai` {#ai}

*Source: `src/ai/mod.rs`*

Game AI toolkit: FSM, Behavior Trees, Steering, Pathfinding, Q-Learning, and more.

All subsystems are decoupled: agents can be driven by FSM, BT, SteeringManager, or any mix.
All computation is pure CPU math — no GPU, audio, or window access required.

---

### `mod agent`  · [line 7](src/ai/mod.rs#L7)

Autonomous agent with pluggable decision models.

---

### `mod behavior_tree`  · [line 9](src/ai/mod.rs#L9)

Behavior tree nodes (sequence, selector, parallel, decorators).

---

### `mod blackboard`  · [line 11](src/ai/mod.rs#L11)

Shared key-value store for inter-agent communication.

---

### `mod command_queue`  · [line 13](src/ai/mod.rs#L13)

Queue-based action scheduling with undo support.

---

### `mod flowfield`  · [line 15](src/ai/mod.rs#L15)

Dijkstra-based flow field for crowd pathfinding.

---

### `mod fsm`  · [line 17](src/ai/mod.rs#L17)

Finite state machine with named states and transitions.

---

### `mod goap`  · [line 19](src/ai/mod.rs#L19)

Goal-oriented action planning (GOAP) solver.

---

### `mod influence_map`  · [line 21](src/ai/mod.rs#L21)

Grid-based influence map for spatial reasoning.

---

### `mod pathgrid`  · [line 23](src/ai/mod.rs#L23)

Weighted grid pathfinding (A*, Dijkstra) with obstacle support.

---

### `mod qlearner`  · [line 25](src/ai/mod.rs#L25)

Tabular Q-learning agent for reinforcement learning.

---

### `mod squad`  · [line 27](src/ai/mod.rs#L27)

Squad coordination: formation, morale, and group behaviour.

---

### `mod steering`  · [line 29](src/ai/mod.rs#L29)

Steering behaviours (seek, flee, wander, flocking, etc.).

---

### `mod utility_ai`  · [line 31](src/ai/mod.rs#L31)

Utility-AI scorer with weighted action selection.

---

### `mod world`  · [line 33](src/ai/mod.rs#L33)

Spatial AI world with team assignment and awareness radius.

---

### `fn QLearner::learn`  · [line 107](src/ai/qlearner.rs#L107)

Bellman update: Q(s,a) ← Q(s,a) + α\[r + γ max Q(s',a') - Q(s,a)\]

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn learn(&mut self, state: usize, action: usize, reward: f64, next_state: usize)
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `state` | `usize`. |
| `action` | `usize`. |
| `reward` | `f64`. |
| `next_state` | `usize`. |

---

### `fn QLearner::end_episode`  · [line 121](src/ai/qlearner.rs#L121)

Ends the current episode: applies epsilon decay and increments episode count.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn end_episode(&mut self)
```

## Module: `audio::bus` {#audio-bus}

*Source: `src/audio/bus.rs`*

Named audio bus for grouping sources under shared volume, pitch, and pause controls.

---

### `struct Bus`  · [line 9](src/audio/bus.rs#L9)

A named audio bus that applies volume, pitch, and pause overrides to assigned sources.

Buses are pure data containers — they hold no rodio resources. The `Mixer` multiplies a source's per-source volume/pitch by its assigned bus values. Setting a bus to paused suppresses playback of all assigned sources.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct Bus
```

**Fields:**

| Field | Type | Description |
|-------|------|-------------|
| `name` | | *(private)* |
| `volume` | | *(private)* |
| `pitch` | | *(private)* |
| `paused` | | *(private)* |

---

Software MIDI synthesizer: parses MIDI with `midly`, renders to PCM
via sine-additive synthesis, and plays through a rodio `Sink`.

---

### `struct MidiPlayer`  · [line 44](src/audio/midi_player.rs#L44)

Software MIDI player with sine-additive synthesis.

Parses MIDI via `midly`, renders all tracks to a PCM buffer on `play()`, and feeds the result into a `rodio::Sink`. Supports per-channel volume, muting, track muting, tempo scaling, and looping.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct MidiPlayer
```

**Fields:**

| Field | Type | Description |
|-------|------|-------------|
| `midi_data` | | *(private)* |
| `raw_midi` | | *(private)* |
| `file_path` | | *(private)* |
| `volume` | | *(private)* |
| `looping` | | *(private)* |
| `tempo_scale` | | *(private)* |
| `current_bpm` | | *(private)* |
| `channel_muted` | | *(private)* |
| `channel_volume` | | *(private)* |
| `channel_instrument` | | *(private)* |
| `track_muted` | | *(private)* |
| `position_secs` | | *(private)* |
| `sink` | | *(private)* |
| `play_state` | | *(private)* |
| `bus_key` | | *(private)* |

## Module: `audio::mixer` {#audio-mixer}

*Source: `src/audio/mixer.rs`*

Core audio mixer that owns every loaded sound and drives playback through rodio.

[`Mixer`] is the single point of entry for all audio operations in Luna2D.  It opens the
system's default output stream on construction (via rodio) and maintains a slot-map of
[`AudioEntry`] records — one per loaded sound.  Each entry embeds a `rodio::Sink` for
playback control and cached metadata (duration, fade parameters, loop flag, filters).

# Source types

The mixer supports two loading strategies selected at load time:
- **Static** — the raw file bytes are decoded and held in an `Arc<Vec<u8>>` inside the
  entry.  Playback restarts by re-decoding from that in-memory buffer, giving very low
  latency at the cost of higher RAM usage.  Best for short sound effects.
- **Stream** — the file is opened fresh from disk on each play call and decoded
  incrementally.  Lower memory overhead for long music tracks.

# Bus routing

Every sound can be assigned to a named audio bus stored in a secondary slot-map.
Volume and pitch for a playing source are the product of the per-source values and the
values of its assigned bus.  Setting a bus to paused suspends every source on that bus.

# Master volume

A single master-volume scalar is applied on top of all per-source and per-bus volumes,
letting game code provide a global volume slider without touching individual sources.

# Time tracking

Because rodio `Sink` does not expose a playback position, the mixer tracks play-start
instants and accumulated pre-pause seconds manually so `luna.audio.getTime` can return
the current position in the stream.

Manages audio output via rodio: loads sources, controls playback, and adjusts volume.

Supports static (in-memory) and streaming source types, per-source volume/pitch/pan, master volume, looping, batch operations, and source cloning.

**Returns:** `Option<f32>`. For static sources, duration is populated on first `play` call. Returns `None` if the source has never been played or if the decoder could not determine the duration (e.g. some streaming formats).

---

### `fn Mixer::get_tell`  · [line 763](src/audio/mixer.rs#L763)

Returns the approximate current playback position in seconds.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn get_tell(&self, key: SoundKey) -> f32
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `key` | `SoundKey`. |

**Returns:** `f32`. Based on wall-clock elapsed time. Returns `0.0` for stopped sources or invalid keys. When playing, includes accumulated time from previous play segments plus time elapsed since the last `play` or `resume`.

---

## Module: `audio` {#audio}

*Source: `src/audio/mod.rs`*

Audio subsystem for Luna2D games.

This module provides sound loading, playback, and volume management through
a [`Mixer`] that wraps the [rodio](https://crates.io/crates/rodio) audio library.
Game code accesses audio through the `luna.audio` Lua bindings in [`crate::lua_api`],
which delegates all work to [`Mixer`] and [`Bus`] instances stored in `SharedState`.

# Key types

- [`Mixer`] — central audio mixer; manages all loaded sounds, their playback state,
  volume, pitch, pan, looping, and fade effects.
- [`Bus`] — named group that applies a shared volume and pause state to every source
  assigned to it (e.g. a "music" bus or "sfx" bus).
- [`AudioSource`] — lightweight handle for a loaded audio file, carrying the path and
  default playback settings.
- [`SourceType`] — controls whether a sound is decoded fully into memory (`Static`) or
  read incrementally from disk during playback (`Stream`).
- [`PlayState`] — the current playback status of a source: `Stopped`, `Playing`, or `Paused`.

# Design notes

Buses are pure data containers; the mixer multiplies source volume/pitch by bus values on
every `set_volume` or `update` call.  Audio sources are tracked in a slot-map keyed by
[`crate::engine::resource_keys::SoundKey`], giving O(1) lookup and safe handle
invalidation when sources are released.

---

### `mod bus`  · [line 28](src/audio/mod.rs#L28)

Named audio bus for grouping sources under shared volume/pitch/pause controls.

---

### `mod midi_player`  · [line 30](src/audio/mod.rs#L30)

Software MIDI synthesizer with sine-additive PCM rendering.

---

### `mod mixer`  · [line 32](src/audio/mod.rs#L32)

Low-level audio mixer using rodio for playback and volume control.

---

### `mod source`  · [line 34](src/audio/mod.rs#L34)

Audio source handle holding path, volume, and loop settings.

---

### `mod sound_data`  · [line 43](src/audio/mod.rs#L43)

Decoded PCM sample buffer with per-sample read/write access.

---

### `mod midi`  · [line 47](src/audio/mod.rs#L47)

MIDI SoundFont state management.

```rust
pub struct DeckBuilder
```

| `banned_types` | `Vec<String>` | Banned card types. |

### `struct NdArray`  · [line 71](src/compute/array.rs#L71)

Dense N-dimensional numerical array with row-major strides.

Data is stored as a contiguous `Vec<u8>` byte buffer. Shapes are limited to 1D, 2D, or 3D with a hard cap of 268,435,456 elements.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct NdArray
```

**Fields:**

| Field | Type | Description |
|-------|------|-------------|
| `shape` | | *(private)* |
| `strides` | | *(private)* |
| `dtype` | | *(private)* |
| `data` | | *(private)* |

### `fn NdArray::compute_strides`  · [line 361](src/compute/array.rs#L361)

Compute row-major strides for a given shape.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn compute_strides(shape: &[usize]) -> Vec<usize>
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `shape` | `&[usize]`. |

**Returns:** `Vec<usize>`. `strides[i] = product(shape[i+1..])` — so the last axis has stride 1.

---


## Module: `compute` {#compute}

*Source: `src/compute/mod.rs`*

Dense N-dimensional numerical arrays with NumPy-style operations.

Provides `NdArray` for 1D/2D/3D row-major arrays with float32, float64,
and int32 element types. Used by the `luna.compute` Lua module.

---

### `mod array`  · [line 7](src/compute/mod.rs#L7)

N-dimensional array storage with typed element access.

---

### `mod ops`  · [line 9](src/compute/mod.rs#L9)

Element-wise and reduction operations on NdArray.

---

### `mod spatial`  · [line 11](src/compute/mod.rs#L11)

Spatial operations: convolution, pooling, distance transforms.

---


## Module: `compute::ops` {#compute-ops}

*Source: `src/compute/ops.rs`*

Element-wise, reduction, comparison, masking, shape, and bitwise operations on NdArray.

## Module: `compute::spatial` {#compute-spatial}

*Source: `src/compute/spatial.rs`*

2D spatial operations and linear algebra for NdArray.

---

### `fn convolve2d`  · [line 18](src/compute/spatial.rs#L18)

2D convolution with zero-padding (same-size output).

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn convolve2d(input: &NdArray, kernel: &NdArray) -> Result<NdArray, String>
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `input` | `&NdArray`. |
| `kernel` | `&NdArray`. |

**Returns:** `Result<NdArray, String>`. The kernel center is at `(kR/2, kC/2)`. Both input and kernel must be 2D arrays. Output shape equals input shape.

---

### `fn dilate`  · [line 74](src/compute/spatial.rs#L74)

Morphological dilation with a Manhattan-diamond structuring element.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn dilate(a: &NdArray, radius: usize) -> Result<NdArray, String>
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `a` | `&NdArray`. |
| `radius` | `usize`. |

**Returns:** `Result<NdArray, String>`. For each cell, output is 1.0 if any cell within Manhattan distance `radius` is non-zero in the input, 0.0 otherwise. Input must be 2D.

---

### `fn erode`  · [line 121](src/compute/spatial.rs#L121)

Morphological erosion with a Manhattan-diamond structuring element.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn erode(a: &NdArray, radius: usize) -> Result<NdArray, String>
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `a` | `&NdArray`. |
| `radius` | `usize`. |

**Returns:** `Result<NdArray, String>`. For each cell, output is 1.0 only if all cells within Manhattan distance `radius` are non-zero in the input, 0.0 otherwise. Input must be 2D.

---

### `fn flood_fill`  · [line 173](src/compute/spatial.rs#L173)

Flood fill using BFS with 4-connectivity.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn flood_fill(a: &NdArray, row: usize, col: usize, val: f64) -> Result<NdArray, String>
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `a` | `&NdArray`. |
| `row` | `usize`. |
| `col` | `usize`. |
| `val` | `f64`. |

**Returns:** `Result<NdArray, String>`. Starting from `(row, col)`, fills all connected cells that have the same value as the starting cell with `val`. Returns a new array (does not mutate the original). Indices are 0-based.

---

### `fn get_region`  · [line 231](src/compute/spatial.rs#L231)

Extract a rectangular sub-region from a 2D array.

**Signature:**

**Returns:** `Result<NdArray, String>`. Returns a new 2D array of shape `(sub_rows, sub_cols)` starting at `(row, col)`. All indices are 0-based.

### `fn matmul`  · [line 315](src/compute/spatial.rs#L315)

```rust
pub fn matmul(a: &NdArray, b: &NdArray) -> Result<NdArray, String>
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `a` | `&NdArray`. |
| `b` | `&NdArray`. |

**Returns:** `Result<NdArray, String>`. Uses a naive triple loop. Both arrays must be 2D with compatible inner dimensions.

## Module: `data` {#data}

*Source: `src/data/mod.rs`*

Binary data manipulation, compression, hashing, and encoding.

Provides `ByteData` for raw byte buffers, plus compression (deflate/gzip/lz4/zlib),
cryptographic hashing (MD5/SHA family), and encoding (base64/hex).
Also includes TOML parsing and encoding.

---

### `mod byte_data`  · [line 8](src/data/mod.rs#L8)

Raw byte buffer for binary data manipulation.

---

### `mod compress`  · [line 10](src/data/mod.rs#L10)

---

### `mod encode`  · [line 12](src/data/mod.rs#L12)

Base64 and hex encoding/decoding.

---

### `mod hash`  · [line 14](src/data/mod.rs#L14)

Cryptographic hash functions (MD5, SHA-1, SHA-256, SHA-512).

## Module: `data::toml_convert` {#data-toml-convert}

*Source: `src/data/toml_convert.rs`*

TOML parsing and encoding for Luna2D.

Converts between TOML strings and Lua tables. Supports the full TOML spec
via the `toml` crate, mapping types to their Lua equivalents.

## Module: `dataframe` {#dataframe}

*Source: `src/dataframe/mod.rs`*

In-memory column-major tabular data with query, analytics, and SQL.

Provides `DataFrame` for named-column data tables and `Database` for
multi-table catalogs. Used by the `luna.dataframe` Lua module.

---

### `mod frame`  · [line 7](src/dataframe/mod.rs#L7)

Column-major DataFrame and Database types.

---

### `mod query`  · [line 9](src/dataframe/mod.rs#L9)

Filter, sort, group-by, and aggregate query engine.

---

### `mod serial`  · [line 11](src/dataframe/mod.rs#L11)

CSV and JSON serialization/deserialization for DataFrames.

---

### `mod sql`  · [line 13](src/dataframe/mod.rs#L13)

SQL query parser and executor for in-memory databases.

---

## Module: `dialog` {#dialog}

*Source: `src/dialog/mod.rs`*

Dialog sequencer for visual novel-style text presentation.

Provides a state-machine-based dialog sequencer with typewriter effect,
branching choices, timed pauses, and inline callbacks. Drives text-based
narrative sequences from flat script arrays.

|---------|-------------|
| `Say` | A spoken line with speaker name and text. |
| `Choice` | A branching choice with prompt and options. |
| `Wait` | A timed pause in seconds. |
| `Call` | An inline callback index (resolved by the Lua layer). |

```rust
pub enum SequencerState
```

| `Typing` | Typewriter actively revealing text. |
| `Waiting` | Full text shown; awaiting advance(). |
| `Choice` | Presenting choices; awaiting choose(). |
| `Paused` | Executing a wait node; timer running. |
| `Done` | Script finished. |

## Module: `engine::config` {#engine-config}

*Source: `src/engine/config.rs`*

Engine and window configuration loaded from `conf.lua`.

When the engine starts it looks for a `conf.lua` file in the game directory.
If found, it is executed in a minimal Lua VM and the result is read into a [`Config`]
struct.  Missing fields fall back to built-in defaults so authors only need to specify
the settings they actually want to change.

# Structure

[`Config`] is the top-level container and contains four nested structs:
- [`WindowConfig`] — window geometry, title, display placement, and decoration options.
- [`ModulesConfig`] — boolean feature-flags for optional engine subsystems (audio,
  physics, graphics, etc.).  Disabling a module avoids the startup cost and prevents
  the matching `luna.*` API calls from being registered.
- [`PerformanceConfig`] — target frame-rate cap (`fps_cap`).

The `identity` field sets the name of the per-user save directory returned by
`luna.filesystem.getSaveDirectory()`.  If unset, the engine uses the game directory
name as a fallback.

# Example `conf.lua`

```lua
luna.window.setTitle("My Game")
luna.window.setDimensions(1280, 720)
luna.window.setFullscreen(false)
luna.window.setVsync(true)
```

---

### `struct Config`  · [line 45](src/engine/config.rs#L45)

Top-level engine configuration.

Can be populated from `conf.lua` or constructed with defaults.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct Config
```

**Fields:**

| Field | Description |
|-------|-------------|
| `window` | Window dimensions, title, vsync, fullscreen, and resize settings. |
| `modules` | Flags enabling optional subsystems (audio, physics, graphics, etc.). |
| `performance` | Frame rate cap. |
| `identity` | Save directory name (used for persistent game data). |
| `version` | Target engine version string. |

---

### `struct WindowConfig`  · [line 72](src/engine/config.rs#L72)

Window dimensions, title, vsync, fullscreen, and resize settings.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct WindowConfig
```

**Fields:**

| Field | Description |
|-------|-------------|
| `width` | Window width in pixels. |
| `height` | Window height in pixels. |
| `title` | Title bar string. |
| `vsync` | Enable vertical sync. |
| `fullscreen` | Launch in fullscreen mode. |
| `resizable` | Allow the user to resize the window. |
| `min_width` | Minimum window width (optional). |
| `min_height` | Minimum window height (optional). |
| `borderless` | Remove window decorations (title bar, borders). |
| `icon` | Path to a window icon image, resolved relative to the game directory and applied during startup. |
| `display_index` | Monitor index for window placement (0 = primary). |

---

### `fn Config::load_from_conf_lua`  · [line 170](src/engine/config.rs#L170)

Loads engine configuration from `conf.lua` in the game directory.

If `conf.lua` is absent or contains errors, returns `Config::default()` silently. The expected Lua pattern is: ```lua function luna.conf(t)     t.window.title = "My Game"     t.window.width = 1280     t.window.height = 720 end ```

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn load_from_conf_lua(game_dir: &Path) -> (Self, Option<String>)
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `game_dir` | Absolute path to the directory containing `conf.lua` (and `main.lua`). |

**Returns:** A tuple of `(Config, Option<String>)`. The second element is `Some(msg)` if `conf.lua` had errors; the returned `Config` still holds usable defaults.

## Module: `engine::error` {#engine-error}

*Source: `src/engine/error.rs`*

Structured error types and result alias for the Luna2D engine.

All engine-level error conditions are expressed as variants of [`EngineError`], a
`thiserror`-derived enum that carries a human-readable description and belongs to one
of the six [`ErrorCategory`] groups: `Init`, `Runtime`, `Resource`, `Script`,
`System`, or `Filesystem`.

This module also provides [`EngineResult<T>`], a type alias for
`Result<T, EngineError>`, which should be used in public APIs that can fail.

# Design goal

Every error variant has a stable four-digit numeric code (e.g. `E1001`) that can be
displayed in the error screen and referenced in documentation without changing across
releases.  This makes it straightforward for users to search for a specific error online
or in the Luna2D issue tracker.

Lua errors are wrapped as [`EngineError::LuaError`] so they can flow through the same
result type and be presented by [`crate::engine::error_screen::ErrorScreen`].

---

### `enum ErrorCategory`  · [line 32](src/engine/error.rs#L32)

Error category for grouping related engine errors.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub enum ErrorCategory
```

**Variants:**

| Variant | Description |
|---------|-------------|
| `Init` | Init variant. |
| `Runtime` | Runtime variant. |
| `Resource` | Resource variant. |
| `Script` | Script variant. |
| `System` | System variant. |

---

### `fn ErrorCategory::as_str`  · [line 50](src/engine/error.rs#L50)

Returns the category name as a lowercase string.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn as_str(&self) -> &'static str
```

**Returns:** `&'static str`.

---

### `enum EngineError`  · [line 80](src/engine/error.rs#L80)

All possible error conditions that can occur in the Luna2D engine.

Each variant carries a stable error code (`E1001`–`E1012`) and belongs to an [`ErrorCategory`] for structured error reporting.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub enum EngineError
```

**Variants:**

| Variant | Description |
|---------|-------------|
| `InitializationError` | Engine startup failure (window, renderer, Lua VM). |
| `RenderError` | Error during frame rendering. |
| `InputError` | Error reading or processing input state. |
| `AudioError` | Failure in the audio subsystem. |
| `PhysicsError` | Error in the physics world or body simulation. |
| `FileSystemError` | Sandboxed I/O failure. |
| `LuaError` | Lua script execution or binding error. |
| `WindowError` | Window creation or event loop failure. |
| `ConfigError` | `conf.lua` parse error. |
| `ResourceNotFound` | A requested asset was not found in the game directory. |
| `ResourceNotLoaded` | A resource was released but a stale handle was accessed. |
| `IoError` | Low-level I/O error (from `std::io::Error`). |

---

### `fn EngineError::code`  · [line 123](src/engine/error.rs#L123)

Returns the stable error code for this variant.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn code(&self) -> &'static str
```

**Returns:** `&'static str`.

---


---


**Returns:** Wraps any value type `T` in a `Result` that carries an `EngineError` on failure.

## Module: `engine::log_messages` {#engine-log-messages}

*Source: `src/engine/log_messages.rs`*

Structured logging with stable message IDs for the Luna2D engine.

Every engine log message has a stable ID (`L001`..`L099`) so that external
tools and Lua scripts can filter or match on them.  Use the [`log_msg!`]
macro instead of bare `log::info!` / `log::warn!` / `log::error!` calls.

---

## Module: `engine` {#engine}

*Source: `src/engine/mod.rs`*

Core engine lifecycle: application loop, configuration, error handling, and diagnostics.

This module owns the highest-level runtime structures in the Luna2D engine.
[`App`] drives the winit event loop, fires `luna.load/update/draw/keypressed/…` Lua
callbacks at the right moments, and holds every domain subsystem inside a
`Rc<RefCell<SharedState>>` that is shared with the Lua VM.

# Module overview

- [`app`] — [`App`] struct that implements `winit::ApplicationHandler`.  It creates the
  window and renderer, initialises every subsystem, executes `main.lua`, and routes
  window events to their corresponding Lua callbacks.
- [`config`] — [`Config`], [`WindowConfig`], [`ModulesConfig`], and [`PerformanceConfig`]
  structs loaded from `conf.lua` at startup.
- [`debug_overlay`] — on-screen FPS and draw-call counter drawn in the bottom-right
  corner of the window during development.
- [`error`] — [`EngineError`] enum and [`EngineResult`] type alias used throughout the
  codebase for structured, recoverable error propagation.
- [`error_screen`] — fallback render path that displays a human-readable Lua or engine
  error on screen instead of crashing silently.
- [`log_messages`] — structured, stable-ID log message constants used by `log::info!`
  macros across the engine so message IDs remain consistent between builds.
- [`resource_keys`] — typed newtype keys (`SoundKey`, `TextureKey`, `ShaderId`, …) for
  all slot-map resource pools in the engine.

---

### `mod app`  · [line 27](src/engine/mod.rs#L27)

Entry point for the Luna2D engine lifecycle and game loop.

---

### `mod config`  · [line 29](src/engine/mod.rs#L29)

Engine and window configuration structs (Config, WindowConfig, etc.).

---

### `mod debug_overlay`  · [line 31](src/engine/mod.rs#L31)

## Module: `engine::resource_keys` {#engine-resource-keys}

*Source: `src/engine/resource_keys.rs`*

accidental cross-pool lookups at compile time.

## Module: `event` {#event}

*Source: `src/event/mod.rs`*

Event queue for polling system and custom events.

Provides an alternative to the callback model where game code can poll events
from a FIFO queue. Also contains the `Signal` pub-sub type for handle-based
event dispatching.

---

| `Bool` | Bool variant. |
| `Nil` | Nil variant. |

## Module: `event::signal` {#event-signal}

*Source: `src/event/signal.rs`*

Handle-based pub-sub signal system.

`Signal` provides a lightweight event bus where listeners subscribe by
name and receive a monotonically increasing handle ID for later removal.
Callbacks fire in registration order.

---

### `struct Subscription`  · [line 11](src/event/signal.rs#L11)

A single subscription entry in a [`Signal`].

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct Subscription
```

**Fields:**

| Field | Type | Description |
|-------|------|-------------|
| `handle` | `u64` | Unique handle ID (monotonic, per-Signal instance). |
| `name` | `String` | The event name this subscription listens to. |

---

### `struct Signal`  · [line 25](src/event/signal.rs#L25)

Handle-based pub-sub signal dispatcher.

Listeners register for named events and receive a unique handle ID. When an event is emitted, all matching callbacks fire in registration order. The actual callback functions are stored externally (e.g. in the Lua registry); this struct tracks only the subscription metadata.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct Signal
```

**Fields:**

| Field | Type | Description |
|-------|------|-------------|
| `next_handle` | | *(private)* |
| `subscriptions` | | *(private)* |
| `handle_to_name` | | *(private)* |

---

### `fn Signal::new`  · [line 36](src/event/signal.rs#L36)

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn new() -> Self
```

---

**Signature:**


## Module: `filesystem::async_loader` {#filesystem-async-loader}

*Source: `src/filesystem/async_loader.rs`*

Background asset-loading worker that reads files off the main thread.

The loader owns a single OS thread that processes read requests from a bounded
channel.  Results are polled from the main thread each frame — no `unsafe`, no
shared mutable state beyond an `Arc<Mutex<>>` result map.

---

### `struct LoadHandle`  · [line 15](src/filesystem/async_loader.rs#L15)

Opaque handle returned to callers (and to Lua) that identifies a pending load.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct LoadHandle
```

---

### `enum LoadResult`  · [line 23](src/filesystem/async_loader.rs#L23)

Outcome of a completed load request.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub enum LoadResult
```

**Variants:**

| Variant | Description |
|---------|-------------|
| `Ready` | Ready variant. |
| `Error` | Error variant. |

---

### `enum LoadStatus`  · [line 36](src/filesystem/async_loader.rs#L36)

Status returned by [`AsyncLoader::poll`].

**Signature:**
```rust
pub enum LoadStatus
```

**Variants:**

| Variant | Description |
|---------|-------------|
| `Pending` | Pending variant. |
| `Done` | Done variant. |

---

### `struct AsyncLoader`  · [line 56](src/filesystem/async_loader.rs#L56)

A single-threaded background file reader.

Create one per engine session; drop it to join the worker thread.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct AsyncLoader
```

**Fields:**

| Field | Type | Description |
|-------|------|-------------|
| `next_id` | | *(private)* |
| `tx` | | *(private)* |
| `results` | | *(private)* |


**Returns:** `Self`.

---

### `fn AsyncLoader::request_load`  · [line 101](src/filesystem/async_loader.rs#L101)

Submit a file-read request.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn request_load(&self, resolved_path: PathBuf) -> LoadHandle
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `resolved_path` | `PathBuf`. |

**Returns:** `LoadHandle`. `resolved_path` must already be sandbox-validated (canonical, inside the game directory).  Path validation is the caller's responsibility and MUST happen on the main thread *before* this call to prevent TOCTOU races. Returns a [`LoadHandle`] that can be passed to [`poll`](Self::poll).

---

### `fn AsyncLoader::poll`  · [line 133](src/filesystem/async_loader.rs#L133)

Check the status of a previously-requested load.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn poll(&self, handle: LoadHandle) -> LoadStatus
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `handle` | `LoadHandle`. |

**Returns:** `LoadStatus`. Returns [`LoadStatus::Done`] exactly once — subsequent polls for the same handle return [`LoadStatus::Pending`] (the entry is removed on first read).

---

### `fn AsyncLoader::pending_results`  · [line 146](src/filesystem/async_loader.rs#L146)

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn pending_results(&self) -> usize
```

**Returns:** `usize`.

### `fn GameFS::read_string`  · [line 81](src/filesystem/vfs.rs#L81)

Reads the file at `path` (relative to base dir) and returns its contents as a `String`.

Canonicalises the path and rejects any path that escapes the base directory, preventing path-traversal attacks.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn read_string(&self, path: &str) -> EngineResult<String>
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `path` | Relative path to the file within the game directory. |

**Returns:** `Ok(String)` — The UTF-8 file contents. `Err(EngineError)` — I/O or traversal error.

---

### `fn GameFS::read_bytes`  · [line 109](src/filesystem/vfs.rs#L109)


**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `path` | Relative path to the file within the game directory. |

**Returns:** `Ok(Vec<u8>)` — The raw file bytes. `Err(EngineError)` — I/O or traversal error.

---

### `fn GameFS::write_string`  · [line 138](src/filesystem/vfs.rs#L138)

Writes `content` to `path`, which must be inside the `save/` subdirectory.

Creates parent directories automatically. Rejects any path outside `save/` to prevent scripts from writing arbitrary files to the system.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn write_string(&self, path: &str, content: &str) -> EngineResult<()>
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `path` | Relative path under `save/`, e.g. `"save/progress.json"`. |
| `content` | String content to write. |

**Returns:** `Ok(())` on success. `Err(EngineError)` if the path is outside `save/` or an I/O error occurs.

## Module: `graph` {#graph}

*Source: `src/graph/mod.rs`*

Directed graph with item flow simulation for Luna2D.

Provides nodes, edges, typed items, simulation (decay, transit, push/pull flow,
conversions, queues), Dijkstra pathfinding, graph algorithms (components, cycles,
topological sort), and supply/demand processing.

---

### `mod algorithms`  · [line 8](src/graph/mod.rs#L8)

Graph algorithms: connected components, topological sort, cycle detection.

---

### `mod core`  · [line 10](src/graph/mod.rs#L10)

Core `Graph` struct — nodes, edges, and item storage.

---

Directed edge with capacity, cooldown, and type-filtering.

---

Typed items that flow through the graph.

## Module: `graph::supply_demand` {#graph-supply-demand}

Supply/demand processing — match demands to supplies and route items.

---

### `fn Graph::process_demand`  · [line 16](src/graph/supply_demand.rs#L16)

Process all demand/supply declarations.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn process_demand(&mut self) -> Vec<GraphEvent>
```

**Returns:** `Vec<GraphEvent>`. Iterates demand nodes in priority order (highest first), finds matching supply nodes via pathfinding, creates items at the supply and routes them. Returns events for callback dispatch.

---

## Module: `graphics::animation` {#graphics-animation}

*Source: `src/graphics/animation.rs`*

Sprite animation system with named clips, speed control, and frame-level events.

An [`Animation`] stores a pool of [`AnimFrame`] entries (each defining a source
rectangle and optional per-frame duration) and any number of named [`AnimClip`]s
that reference those frames by index. Call [`Animation::update`] each tick and
inspect [`Animation::drain_events`] for playback notifications.

---

### `type AnimationFrame`  · [line 18](src/graphics/animation.rs#L18)

Backward-compatible alias for [`AnimFrame`].

Existing code that imports `AnimationFrame` from `crate::graphics` will continue to compile after the Phase 24 rewrite.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub type AnimationFrame = AnimFrame
```

---

---

### `struct Animation`  · [line 90](src/graphics/animation.rs#L90)

Sprite animation with named clips, speed control, and playback events.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct Animation
```

**Usage:**

1. Add frames with [`add_frame`](Self::add_frame) or
   [`add_frames_from_grid`](Self::add_frames_from_grid).
2. Register one or more clips with [`add_clip`](Self::add_clip).
3. Call [`play`](Self::play) to start a clip, then
   [`update`](Self::update) each tick.
4. Read the current source quad via [`current_quad`](Self::current_quad).

**Fields:**

| Field | Type | Description |
|-------|------|-------------|
| `frames` | | *(private)* |
| `clips` | | *(private)* |
| `current_clip` | | *(private)* |
| `current_frame_pos` | | *(private)* |
| `timer` | | *(private)* |
| `playing` | | *(private)* |
| `speed` | | *(private)* |
| `pending_events` | | *(private)* |

---

### `fn Animation::current_quad`  · [line 372](src/graphics/animation.rs#L372)

Returns the source rectangle of the current frame, or `None` if no

**Signature:**

```rust
pub fn current_quad(&self) -> Option<Rect>
```

## Module: `graphics::camera` {#graphics-camera}

*Source: `src/graphics/camera.rs`*

Camera types for 2D viewport control.

Provides the original [`Camera`] (used by `SharedState` for the flat
`luna.graphics.setCamera()` API) and the new Phase 24 [`Camera2D`] with
smooth follow, dead zone, bounds clamping, and screen-shake.

---

### `struct Camera`  · [line 21](src/graphics/camera.rs#L21)

Basic camera with position, zoom, and rotation.

Used by `SharedState` for the flat `luna.graphics.setCamera()` API.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct Camera
```

**Fields:**

| Field | Description |
|-------|-------------|
| `position` | World-space centre point the camera is looking at. |
| `zoom` | Uniform scale factor; `1.0` = natural size, `2.0` = 2x zoom in. |
| `rotation` | Rotation in radians, applied after zoom. |

---

### `fn Camera::new`  · [line 40](src/graphics/camera.rs#L40)

Creates a new `Camera` with the given position, zoom, and rotation.

**Signature:**
```rust

```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `position` | `Vec2`. |
| `zoom` | `f32`. |
| `rotation` | `f32`. |

**Returns:** `Self`.

---

### `fn Camera::view_matrix`  · [line 55](src/graphics/camera.rs#L55)

Computes the view transformation matrix for this camera.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn view_matrix(&self) -> Mat3
```

**Returns:** `Mat3`. Combines translation (negate position), rotation, and scale (zoom) into a single `Mat3`.

## Module: `graphics::canvas` {#graphics-canvas}

*Source: `src/graphics/canvas.rs`*

Off-screen render targets (canvases) for deferred compositing.

A `Canvas` stores the logical dimensions of an off-screen texture that the
GPU renderer can draw to.  After rendering, the canvas can be composited to
the screen (or another canvas) as a regular image.

---

### `struct Canvas`  · [line 16](src/graphics/canvas.rs#L16)

An off-screen render target with a fixed pixel resolution.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct Canvas
```

**Fields:**

| Field | Description |
|-------|-------------|
| `width` | `u32`. |
| `height` | `u32`. |

---

**Returns:** `Self`.

## Module: `graphics::column_batch` {#graphics-column-batch}

*Source: `src/graphics/column_batch.rs`*

Wolfenstein-style raycasting column batch renderer.

Stores per-column wall data produced by a raycaster and provides
helpers for updating columns from raw ray data and querying depth.

---

## Module: `graphics::data_graph_renderer` {#graphics-data-graph-renderer}

*Source: `src/graphics/data_graph_renderer.rs`*

Mathematical function graph and chart renderer.

[`GraphRenderer`] manages multiple named data series (line, scatter, bar)
and provides viewport ↔ world coordinate mapping for rendering charts in
a Luna2D game. The renderer stores pure data — actual draw calls are
issued by the Lua wrapper in `graphics_api.rs`.

---

### `enum GraphSeries`  · [line 21](src/graphics/data_graph_renderer.rs#L21)

A data series that can be added to a [`GraphRenderer`].

**Signature:**
```rust
pub enum GraphSeries
```

**Variants:**

| Variant | Description |
|---------|-------------|
| `Line` | Line variant. |
| `Scatter` | Scatter variant. |
| `Bar` | Bar variant. |

---

```rust

```

**Returns:** `&str`.

## Module: `graphics::draw_layer` {#graphics-draw-layer}

*Source: `src/graphics/draw_layer.rs`*

Z-ordered draw layer for controlling render order.

Entries are queued with a z-order value and flushed in ascending order
so that lower z-values are drawn first (back-to-front).

---

---

## Module: `graphics::gpu_renderer` {#graphics-gpu-renderer}

*Source: `src/graphics/gpu_renderer.rs`*

GPU-accelerated 2D renderer for Luna2D, backed by wgpu.

Processes a `DrawCommand` queue each frame, tessellates geometry on the CPU,
uploads vertex / index data to GPU buffers, and issues a single render pass.

# Design
- Two render pipelines: *color* (solid + gradient shapes) and *texture* (images, sprites).
- Transform stack maintained during command processing — identical to standard push/pop transform stack.
- Colored geometry is batched in one draw call; each distinct texture source is one draw call.
- Draw order: colored shapes first (in submission order), textured images second.

---

### `struct RenderStats`  · [line 99](src/graphics/gpu_renderer.rs#L99)

Per-frame rendering statistics.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct RenderStats
```

**Fields:**

| Field | Description |
|-------|-------------|
| `draw_calls` | `u32`. |
| `texture_switches` | `u32`. |
| `canvas_switches` | `u32`. |
| `shader_switches` | `u32`. |
| `batched_draws` | `u32`. |

---

## Module: `graphics::large_map_renderer` {#graphics-large-map-renderer}

*Source: `src/graphics/large_map_renderer.rs`*

Optimized renderer for large tile-based maps with chunking and LOD.

[`LargeMapRenderer`] stores a flat tile array and divides it into
[`MapChunk`]s for efficient culling. Dirty flags allow incremental
rebuilds when individual tiles change. The renderer tracks camera
position, zoom, and viewport to compute which chunks are visible.

---

### `struct MapChunk`  · [line 22](src/graphics/large_map_renderer.rs#L22)

A chunk of tiles pre-batched for fast culling and rendering.

|-------|-------------|

| `cy` | `i32`. |
| `dirty` | `bool`. |
| `tile_ids` | `Vec<u32>`. |

## Module: `graphics::nine_slice` {#graphics-nine-slice}

*Source: `src/graphics/nine_slice.rs`*

Nine-slice (9-patch) image rendering for scalable UI elements.

A nine-slice divides a texture into 9 regions using 4 border insets:
corners are drawn at fixed size, edges stretch in one axis, and the
center stretches in both axes. This preserves visual quality when
scaling UI panels, buttons, and dialog boxes.

---

### `type Patch`  · [line 11](src/graphics/nine_slice.rs#L11)

A single patch rectangle: `(src_x, src_y, src_w, src_h, dst_x, dst_y, dst_w, dst_h)`.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub type Patch = (f32, f32, f32, f32, f32, f32, f32, f32)
```

---

### `struct NineSlice`  · [line 33](src/graphics/nine_slice.rs#L33)

A nine-slice image definition: a texture plus border insets.

The four insets (`top`, `right`, `bottom`, `left`) define pixel distances from each edge of the source texture. These divide the texture into 9 regions:

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct NineSlice
```

**Fields:**

| Field | Type | Description |
|-------|------|-------------|
| `texture_key` | `TextureKey` | Key into `SharedState::textures` for the source image. |
| `top` | `f32` | Pixels inset from the top edge. |
| `right` | `f32` | Pixels inset from the right edge. |
| `bottom` | `f32` | Pixels inset from the bottom edge. |
| `left` | `f32` | Pixels inset from the left edge. |
| `tex_width` | `f32` | Full source texture width in pixels. |
| `tex_height` | `f32` | Full source texture height in pixels. |

---

### `fn NineSlice::new`  · [line 64](src/graphics/nine_slice.rs#L64)

Creates a new nine-slice definition.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn new( texture_key: TextureKey, top: f32, right: f32, bottom: f32, left: f32, tex_width: f32, tex_height: f32, ) -> Self
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `texture_key` | Key for the source texture in SharedState. |
| `top` | Pixel inset from the top edge. |
| `right` | Pixel inset from the right edge. |
| `bottom` | Pixel inset from the bottom edge. |
| `left` | Pixel inset from the left edge. |
| `tex_width` | Full source texture width in pixels. |
| `tex_height` | Full source texture height in pixels. |

**Returns:** A new `NineSlice`.

---

### `fn NineSlice::patches`  · [line 96](src/graphics/nine_slice.rs#L96)

Returns the 9 source and destination rectangles for rendering.

Each entry is `(src_x, src_y, src_w, src_h, dst_x, dst_y, dst_w, dst_h)`.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn patches(&self, x: f32, y: f32, w: f32, h: f32) -> [Patch; 9]
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `x` | Destination X position. |
| `y` | Destination Y position. |
| `w` | Destination total width. |
| `h` | Destination total height. |

**Returns:** An array of 9 `Patch` rectangles.

---


## Module: `graphics::palette_lut` {#graphics-palette-lut}

*Source: `src/graphics/palette_lut.rs`*

Color palette lookup table for shader-based palette swapping.

Maps source colors to target colors, allowing sprites to be
re-colored at render time without modifying the original texture.

---

## Module: `graphics::postfx` {#graphics-postfx}

*Source: `src/graphics/postfx.rs`*

Post-processing effects module.

Provides a stackable post-processing pipeline with built-in effects
(bloom, blur, CRT, vignette, chromatic aberration, colour grading,
godrays) and custom shader passes. Effects are organized into a
`PostFxStack` that captures the scene via ping-pong canvases,
applies all enabled effects in order, and outputs the final result.

---

### `enum PostFxEffectType`  · [line 15](src/graphics/postfx.rs#L15)

Built-in effect types for the post-processing pipeline.

Each variant produces a different full-screen shader pass.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub enum PostFxEffectType
```

**Variants:**

| Variant | Description |
|---------|-------------|
| `Bloom` | HDR bloom with threshold + intensity parameters. |
| `Blur` | Gaussian blur with radius parameter. |
| `Crt` | CRT monitor simulation with scanline strength. |
| `Godrays` | Light ray / god ray effect with intensity. |
| `Vignette` | Screen edge darkening with strength. |
| `ColourGrade` | Colour grading / tone mapping. |
| `Chromatic` | Chromatic aberration with offset. |
| `Custom` | Custom shader pass (created via `newPass()`). |

---

### `fn PostFxEffectType::from_name`  · [line 43](src/graphics/postfx.rs#L43)

Parses a string name into an effect type.

**Signature:**
```rust

```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `name` | `&str` — One of `"bloom"`, `"blur"`, `"crt"`, `"godrays"`, |

**Returns:** `Option<Self>` — `None` if the name is unrecognised.

### `enum DrawCommand`  · [line 138](src/graphics/renderer.rs#L138)

A single deferred draw operation queued during `luna.draw()` and executed by `GpuRenderer`.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub enum DrawCommand
```

**Variants:**

| Variant | Description |
|---------|-------------|
| `Rectangle` | Draws an axis-aligned rectangle. |
| `RoundedRectangle` | Draws a rectangle with rounded corners. |
| `Circle` | Draws a circle at center `(x, y)` with radius `r`. |
| `Ellipse` | Draws an ellipse with semi-axes `rx`, `ry`. |
| `Triangle` | Draws a triangle with three explicit vertices. |
| `Polygon` | Draws an arbitrary polygon from a flat `[x0, y0, x1, y1, ...]` vertex list. |
| `Line` | Draws a line segment from `(x1, y1)` to `(x2, y2)`. |
| `Polyline` | Draws a connected sequence of line segments through a flat `[x0,y0,x1,y1,…]` list. |
| `DrawImage` | Blits a texture (by index) at position `(x, y)`. |
| `DrawImageEx` | Draws a texture with full transform (rotation, scale, origin offset). |
| `DrawQuad` | Draws a sub-region (quad) of a texture with full transform. |
| `Print` | Renders text using the built-in bitmap font. |
| `SetLineWidth` | Sets the stroke width for subsequent outline draws. |
| `PushTransform` | Saves the current transform onto the stack. |
| `PopTransform` | Restores the previous transform from the stack. |
| `Translate` | Applies a translation to the current transform. |
| `Rotate` | Applies a rotation (in radians) to the current transform. |
| `Scale` | Applies a scale to the current transform. |
| `Arc` | Draws an arc (sector or outline) of a circle. |

---

## Module: `graphics::sprite` {#graphics-sprite}

*Source: `src/graphics/sprite.rs`*

---

### `struct Sprite`  · [line 15](src/graphics/sprite.rs#L15)

A textured game object with position, scale, rotation, and tint color.

`Sprite` acts as a transform + tint wrapper around a `Texture`. It does not own the texture; it references it by id in the renderer's texture atlas.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct Sprite
```

**Fields:**

| Field | Description |
|-------|-------------|
| `texture_id` | Index into the renderer's texture atlas. |
| `position` | World-space position of the sprite's origin. |
| `scale` | Per-axis scale factor; `Vec2::ONE` = original size. |
| `rotation` | Rotation in radians. |
| `color` | Multiplicative tint applied to the texture; `Color::WHITE` = no tint. |

---

### `fn Sprite::new`  · [line 34](src/graphics/sprite.rs#L34)

## Module: `graphics::sprite_batch` {#graphics-sprite-batch}

Sprite batching for efficient rendering of many sprites sharing one texture.

---

### `struct SpriteBatch`  · [line 9](src/graphics/sprite_batch.rs#L9)

A batch of sprites sharing a single texture, drawn in one GPU call.

Created via `luna.graphics.newSpriteBatch(image_id, max_sprites?)`. Use `add()` to queue sprites and the engine draws them all at once.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct SpriteBatch
```

**Fields:**

| Field | Type | Description |

| `texture_key` | | *(private)* |
| `entries` | | *(private)* |
| `max_entries` | | *(private)* |

## Module: `graphics::sprite_sheet` {#graphics-sprite-sheet}

*Source: `src/graphics/sprite_sheet.rs`*

Grid-based sprite sheet with directional support and named groups.

Splits a texture into a uniform grid of frames and provides indexed,
row/column, named-group, and directional access to the resulting quads.

## Module: `graphics::texture` {#graphics-texture}

*Source: `src/graphics/texture.rs`*

---

### `struct Texture`  · [line 16](src/graphics/texture.rs#L16)

A loaded image asset referenced by its index into the renderer's texture list.

`Texture` is a lightweight handle; the actual pixel data lives in `TextureData` inside `Renderer::textures` (or `SharedState::textures`).

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct Texture
```

**Fields:**

| Field | Description |
|-------|-------------|
| `id` | Index into the renderer's `TextureData` list. |
| `width` | Image width in pixels. |
| `height` | Image height in pixels. |

---

### `fn Texture::load`  · [line 35](src/graphics/texture.rs#L35)

Loads an image from `path`, premultiplies alpha, and appends it to `textures`.

Supports PNG, JPEG, BMP, and any format handled by the `image` crate. Alpha is premultiplied because the GPU renderer expects premultiplied color space.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn load<P: AsRef<Path>>( path: P, textures: &mut SlotMap<TextureKey, TextureData>, ) -> EngineResult<Self>
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `path` | Filesystem path to the image file. |
| `textures` | Mutable texture list; the decoded `TextureData` is pushed here. |

**Returns:** `Ok(Texture)` — Handle with the new id, width, and height. `Err(EngineError)` — Resource not found or image decode error.

---

### `fn Texture::from_rgba`  · [line 81](src/graphics/texture.rs#L81)

Creates a texture from raw RGBA pixel data (not premultiplied).

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn from_rgba( width: u32, height: u32, mut pixels: Vec<u8>, textures: &mut SlotMap<TextureKey, TextureData>, ) -> EngineResult<Self>
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `width` | `u32`. |
| `height` | `u32`. |
| `pixels` | `Vec<u8>`. |
| `textures` | `&mut SlotMap<TextureKey, TextureData>`. |

**Returns:** `EngineResult<Self>`. The data is premultiplied in-place before insertion.

---


## Module: `graphics::texture_atlas` {#graphics-texture-atlas}

*Source: `src/graphics/texture_atlas.rs`*

CPU-side bin-packing texture atlas using a shelf algorithm.

Packs named rectangular regions into a fixed-size atlas without any
GPU interaction. Useful for building sprite-sheet layouts at load time.

---

## Module: `graphics::trail` {#graphics-trail}

*Source: `src/graphics/trail.rs`*

Trail renderer for fading ribbon effects.

Stores a series of timestamped points that age out over a configurable
lifetime, producing a tapered ribbon from head to tail.

---

## Module: `graphics::viewport` {#graphics-viewport}

*Source: `src/graphics/viewport.rs`*

Virtual resolution viewport with manual transform application.

Maps a fixed game resolution onto an arbitrary window size using
letterboxing, stretching, or pixel-perfect scaling.

---

## Module: `image::image_data` {#image-image-data}

*Source: `src/image/image_data.rs`*

CPU-side RGBA8 pixel buffer for image manipulation.

---

### `struct ImageData`  · [line 10](src/image/image_data.rs#L10)

CPU-side pixel buffer in RGBA8 format.

Stores pixel data in row-major order, 4 bytes per pixel (R, G, B, A). Can be created empty, from a file, or from raw bytes.

### `fn winit_key_to_string`  · [line 271](src/input/keyboard.rs#L271)

Converts a `winit 0.30` logical `Key` to the lowercase string name used by the `luna.*` API.

Returns `Some(name)` for recognised keys, `None` for keys without a mapping (which the engine skips silently).

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn winit_key_to_string(key: &winit::keyboard::Key) -> Option<String>
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `key` | A reference to the `winit::keyboard::Key` from a `WindowEvent::KeyboardInput`. |

**Returns:** `Option<String>` — Lowercase key name (e.g. `"space"`, `"escape"`, `"a"`) or `None`.

---

### `fn winit_scancode_to_string`  · [line 322](src/input/keyboard.rs#L322)

Converts a `winit 0.30` physical `KeyCode` to a engine-compatible scancode string.

Scancodes represent physical key positions and are layout-independent.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn winit_scancode_to_string(code: winit::keyboard::KeyCode) -> Option<&'static str>
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `code` | A `winit::keyboard::KeyCode` from the physical key field. |

**Returns:** `Option<&'static str>` — Scancode string or `None` for unmapped keys.

Inventory system — slot-based item containers, equipment slots, item sets,

### `struct Item`  · [line 12](src/inventory/mod.rs#L12)

A single item definition with type, tags, weight, size, and stack limit.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct Item
```

**Fields:**

| Field | Type | Description |
|-------|------|-------------|
| `item_type` | `String` | The item type identifier string. |
| `tags` | `Vec<String>` | Tags applied to the item (e.g. "weapon", "consumable"). |
| `weight` | `f64` | Item weight used by the weight subsystem. |
| `size_w` | `u32` | Width in grid units. |
| `size_h` | `u32` | Height in grid units. |
| `stack_limit` | `u32` | Maximum number of items in a single stack (1 = non-stackable). |

### `struct Inventory`  · [line 464](src/inventory/mod.rs#L464)

Top-level inventory managing containers, equip slots, item sets, and callbacks.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct Inventory
```

**Fields:**

| Field | Type | Description |
|-------|------|-------------|
| `containers` | `HashMap<String, Container>` | Named storage containers. |
| `container_order` | `Vec<String>` | Ordered container name list for deterministic iteration. |
| `equip_slots` | `HashMap<String, Slot>` | Named equipment slots. |
| `equip_slot_order` | `Vec<String>` | Ordered equip slot names. |
| `item_sets` | `Vec<ItemSet>` | Registered item sets. |

## Module: `root` {#root}

*Source: `src/lib.rs`*

Luna2D — a 2D game engine written in Rust that loads and executes Lua game scripts.

This crate is the engine library. It re-exports every subsystem through public submodules so
that the `luna2d` binary, integration tests, and tooling can all share the same code paths.
Game developers do not interact with this crate directly; they write Lua scripts that call
the `luna.*` API, which is registered by [`lua_api`] on top of the types defined here.

# Architecture overview

The engine is split into domain modules with a strict dependency direction:
`engine` may depend on all modules; `lua_api` bridges engine types to the Lua VM;
domain modules (`graphics`, `physics`, `audio`, `input`, `timer`, `filesystem`, `math`,
`window`) must not depend on each other except through `math`.

The main entry point is [`luna_run`], which is called by both the `luna` (console) and
`lunec` (no-console) binaries. It installs the panic hook, parses CLI arguments, loads
`conf.lua`, and enters the main engine loop via [`engine::App::run`].

# Submodule map

| Module | Purpose |
|---|---|
| [`ai`] | FSM, behaviour trees, steering, pathfinding, Q-learning, influence maps |
| [`audio`] | Sound playback via rodio, bus routing, MIDI synthesis |
| [`compute`] | N-dimensional numerical arrays (luna.compute) |
| [`data`] | Binary data, compression, hashing, base64/hex encoding |
| [`dataframe`] | In-memory column-major tabular data |
| [`engine`] | App lifecycle, Config, EngineError, debug overlay |
| [`entity`] | Lightweight ECS with ID recycling, tags, blueprints, systems |
| [`event`] | Event queue for polling and custom events |
| [`filesystem`] | Sandboxed game filesystem (GameFS) |
| [`graph`] | Directed graph with item-flow simulation and pathfinding |
| [`graphics`] | GPU rendering pipeline via wgpu, draw commands, fonts |
| [`image`] | CPU-side RGBA8 pixel buffer for image manipulation |
| [`input`] | Keyboard, mouse, gamepad, and touch input state |
| [`lua_api`] | Lua VM creation and all `luna.*` API bindings |
| [`math`] | Vec2, Mat3, Rect, polygon utilities, pathfinding, raycasting |
| [`modding`] | Mod metadata, dependency resolution, and hook dispatch |
| [`particle`] | Emitter-based 2D particle effects |
| [`physics`] | Rigid bodies, AABB/circle collision, sensors, layer filtering |
| [`savegame`] | Slot-based save/load with schema versioning and auto-save |
| [`scene`] | Scene stack, depth-sorted rendering, visual transitions |
| [`sound`] | Decoded PCM audio sample buffers |
| [`tilemap`] | TileSet, TileMap, autotile, coordinate utilities, map generation |
| [`timer`] | Frame delta-time clock and scheduler |
| [`window`] | winit event-loop wrapper |

## Module: `lua_api::debugbridge_api` {#lua-api-debugbridge-api}

*Source: `src/lua_api/debugbridge_api.rs`*

Registers the `luna.debugbridge.*` TCP debug server API.

Embeds a JSON-over-TCP server (127.0.0.1 only) inside the running game.
External tools (VS Code extension, MCP server) connect to inspect and
control the game at runtime. Network I/O runs on a background thread;
Lua-dependent methods are queued and dispatched via `poll()` on the main thread.

---

### `fn register`  · [line 355](src/lua_api/debugbridge_api.rs#L355)

standard game object type system.

Standard type identification for Luna2D UserData objects.

### `struct SharedState`  · [line 294](src/lua_api/mod.rs#L294)

Shared mutable state passed via `Rc<RefCell<SharedState>>` to all Lua API closures and the engine loop.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct SharedState
```

**Fields:**

| Field | Description |
|-------|-------------|
| `draw_commands` | Queue of pending `DrawCommand` values, flushed each frame. |
| `current_color` | Active RGBA draw color `[r, g, b, a]`. |
| `background_color` | Screen clear color set by `luna.graphics.setBackgroundColor`. |
| `textures` | Loaded texture pixel data, indexed by `Texture::id`. |
| `keys_down` | Set of currently held key name strings. |
| `mouse` | Mouse cursor position, button state, scroll, and cursor settings. |
| `delta_time` | Elapsed time for the current frame in seconds. |
| `total_time` | Accumulated time since engine start in seconds. |
| `fps` | Rolling frames-per-second measurement. |
| `window_width` | Current window width in pixels. |
| `window_height` | Current window height in pixels. |
| `window_title` | Current window title string. |
| `mixer` | The rodio audio mixer managing all sound sources. |
| `game_dir` | Absolute path to the game directory. |
| `quit_requested` | Set to `true` by `luna.event.quit()` to end the game loop. |
| `exit_code` | Exit code to return when `quit_requested` is `true`. |
| `line_width` | Current stroke width for outline draw commands. |
| `blend_mode` | Current blend mode for draw operations. |
| `fonts` | Loaded TTF fonts for text rendering. |
| `active_font` | Index of the currently active font (`None` = use bitmap fallback). |
| `canvases` | Off-screen render targets (canvases) for compositing. |
| `gamepads` | Connected gamepad state instances. |

---

### `fn SharedState::new`  · [line 392](src/lua_api/mod.rs#L392)

Creates a new `SharedState` with the given window dimensions, title, and game directory.

All draw state, timers, and input flags are initialised to safe defaults. The background color defaults to `LUNA_BG` (dark purple).

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn new(width: u32, height: u32, title: &str, game_dir: PathBuf) -> Self
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `width` | Window width in pixels. |
| `height` | Window height in pixels. |
| `title` | Initial window title string. |
| `game_dir` | Absolute path to the game directory. |

**Returns:** A newly-initialised `SharedState`.

---

## Module: `lua_api::scene_api` {#lua-api-scene-api}

*Source: `src/lua_api/scene_api.rs`*

Registers the `luna.scene.*` scene stack, registry, data store, and depth-sorter API.

The scene stack manages a LIFO stack of Lua scene tables with optional
visual transitions. Scene tables are stored via `mlua::RegistryKey` and
identified by `SceneId`. Inter-scene data is stored similarly.

The `DepthSorter` UserData batches draw callbacks by depth for ordered
compositing each frame.

---

## Module: `math::bezier` {#math-bezier}

*Source: `src/math/bezier.rs`*

Bezier curve evaluation using De Casteljau's algorithm.

Supports arbitrary-degree curves with control point manipulation,
rendering to polylines, derivative computation, and geometric transforms.

---

### `struct BezierCurve`  · [line 11](src/math/bezier.rs#L11)

A Bezier curve defined by control points.

Uses De Casteljau's algorithm for evaluation. Minimum 2 control points required.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct BezierCurve
```

**Fields:**

| Field | Type | Description |
|-------|------|-------------|
| `control_points` | | *(private)* |

---

### `fn BezierCurve::new`  · [line 27](src/math/bezier.rs#L27)

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn new(points: Vec<Vec2>) -> Self
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `points` | at least 2 `Vec2` control points defining the curve |

**Returns:** A `BezierCurve` with the given control points.

**Panics:**

Panics if fewer than 2 control points are provided.

---

### `fn BezierCurve::evaluate`  · [line 44](src/math/bezier.rs#L44)

Evaluate the curve at parameter `t` using De Casteljau's algorithm.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn evaluate(&self, t: f32) -> Vec2
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `t` | curve parameter in `[0.0, 1.0]`; 0 returns the first control point, 1 the last |

**Returns:** The point on the curve at `t`.

---

### `fn BezierCurve::render`  · [line 62](src/math/bezier.rs#L62)

```rust

```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `segments` | number of line segments; clamped to at least 1 |

**Returns:** `segments + 1` evenly-spaced `Vec2` points along the curve.

---

### `fn BezierCurve::render_segment`  · [line 81](src/math/bezier.rs#L81)


**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |

| `t_end` | end of the sub-curve parameter in `[0.0, 1.0]` |

**Returns:** `segments + 1` `Vec2` points between `t_start` and `t_end`.

## Module: `math::easing` {#math-easing}

*Source: `src/math/easing.rs`*

Standard easing functions for smooth animation and interpolation.

Each function takes a normalised progress value `t` in `[0.0, 1.0]` and
returns the eased value, also in `[0.0, 1.0]` for most curves.

---

### `fn linear`  · [line 15](src/math/easing.rs#L15)

Linear interpolation — no easing.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn linear(t: f32) -> f32
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `t` | normalised progress value in `[0.0, 1.0]` |

**Returns:** Eased output; typically in `[0.0, 1.0]` (may overshoot for elastic, back, and bounce curves).

---

### `fn apply`  · [line 326](src/math/easing.rs#L326)

Looks up an easing function by name and applies it to progress value `t`.

Supported names (case-insensitive): `"linear"`, `"inQuad"`, `"outQuad"`, `"inOutQuad"`, `"inCubic"`, `"outCubic"`, `"inOutCubic"`, `"inQuart"`, `"outQuart"`, `"inOutQuart"`, `"inSine"`, `"outSine"`, `"inOutSine"`, `"inExpo"`, `"outExpo"`, `"inOutExpo"`, `"inElastic"`, `"outElastic"`, `"outBounce"`, `"inBounce"`, `"inBack"`, `"outBack"`.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn apply(name: &str, t: f32) -> Option<f32>
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `name` | easing name string (case-insensitive) |
| `t` | normalised progress value in `[0.0, 1.0]` |

**Returns:** `Some(f32)` with the eased value, or `None` if the name is unrecognised.

---

polygon operations, and rasterization.

## Module: `math::grid` {#math-grid}

*Source: `src/math/grid.rs`*

2D pathfinding grid with A*, Dijkstra, BFS, and flow field generation.

Cells are addressed with 0-based `(x, y)` coordinates. The Lua layer
converts to/from 1-based indices.

---

### `struct Grid`  · [line 45](src/math/grid.rs#L45)

2D pathfinding grid with per-cell walkability and movement costs.

Supports A*, Dijkstra, and BFS pathfinding as well as flow field generation. All coordinates are 0-based.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct Grid
```

**Fields:**

| Field | Type | Description |
|-------|------|-------------|
| `width` | | *(private)* |
| `height` | | *(private)* |
| `walkable` | | *(private)* |
| `costs` | | *(private)* |

### `fn Grid::find_path_astar`  · [line 203](src/math/grid.rs#L203)

Finds a path from `(sx, sy)` to `(gx, gy)` using A*.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn find_path_astar( &self, sx: u32, sy: u32, gx: u32, gy: u32, diagonal: bool, ) -> Option<Vec<(u32, u32)>>
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `sx` | `u32`. |
| `sy` | `u32`. |
| `gx` | `u32`. |
| `gy` | `u32`. |
| `diagonal` | `bool`. |

**Returns:** `Option<Vec<(u32, u32)>>`. When `diagonal` is `true`, 8-directional movement is allowed and the heuristic uses Euclidean distance; otherwise 4-directional movement with Manhattan distance. Returns `None` if no path exists.

---

### `fn Grid::find_path_dijkstra`  · [line 293](src/math/grid.rs#L293)

Finds a path from `(sx, sy)` to `(gx, gy)` using Dijkstra's algorithm.

**Signature:**

```rust
pub fn find_path_dijkstra( &self, sx: u32, sy: u32, gx: u32, gy: u32, diagonal: bool, ) -> Option<Vec<(u32, u32)>>
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `sx` | `u32`. |
| `sy` | `u32`. |
| `gx` | `u32`. |
| `gy` | `u32`. |
| `diagonal` | `bool`. |

**Returns:** `Option<Vec<(u32, u32)>>`. Equivalent to A* with heuristic = 0. Respects cell costs.

---

### `fn Grid::find_path_bfs`  · [line 373](src/math/grid.rs#L373)

```rust
pub fn find_path_bfs( &self, sx: u32, sy: u32, gx: u32, gy: u32, diagonal: bool, ) -> Option<Vec<(u32, u32)>>
```

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|

| `sy` | `u32`. |
| `gx` | `u32`. |
| `gy` | `u32`. |
| `diagonal` | `bool`. |

**Returns:** `Option<Vec<(u32, u32)>>`. Ignores cell costs — every walkable step has equal weight.

| `gy` | `u32`. |

### `struct Mat3`  · [line 11](src/math/mat3.rs#L11)

A 3×3 column-major matrix used for 2D affine transforms (translation, rotation, scale).

Used by `Camera::view_matrix` to combine position, rotation, and zoom into a single transform that maps world coordinates to screen coordinates.

## Module: `math::noise` {#math-noise}

*Source: `src/math/noise.rs`*

2D Perlin and Simplex noise generators for procedural content.

All functions return values in `[-1.0, 1.0]`. Seed is used to offset the
gradient hash, producing different noise patterns per seed.

---

### `fn perlin2d`  · [line 15](src/math/noise.rs#L15)

Generates 2D Perlin noise at the given coordinates.

**Signature:**
```rust

```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `x` | X coordinate in noise space |
| `y` | Y coordinate in noise space |
| `seed` | numeric seed to vary the noise pattern |

**Returns:** A value in approximately `[-1.0, 1.0]`.

---

### `fn fbm`  · [line 82](src/math/noise.rs#L82)

Generates fractal Brownian motion noise by layering multiple octaves of Perlin noise.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn fbm(x: f32, y: f32, seed: u32, octaves: u32, lacunarity: f32, gain: f32) -> f32
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `x` | X coordinate in noise space |
| `y` | Y coordinate in noise space |
| `seed` | numeric seed |
| `octaves` | number of noise layers (1–8 typical) |
| `lacunarity` | frequency multiplier per octave (typical: 2.0) |
| `gain` | amplitude multiplier per octave (typical: 0.5) |

**Returns:** A value centred around `0.0` in approximately `[-1.0, 1.0]`.

---

### `struct NoiseGenerator`  · [line 556](src/math/noise.rs#L556)

Seeded procedural noise generator.

Holds a 512-entry permutation table derived deterministically from the seed.  All noise methods are pure functions of the seed and coordinates — the same inputs always produce the same output.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct NoiseGenerator
```

**Fields:**

| Field | Type | Description |
|-------|------|-------------|
| `seed` | | *(private)* |
| `perm` | | *(private)* |

### `fn triangulate`  · [line 14](src/math/polygon.rs#L14)

**Signature:**

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `polygon` | slice of `Vec2` vertices forming a simple (non-self-intersecting) polygon; |

**Returns:** `Ok(triangles)` — a `Vec` of `[Vec2; 3]` triangle triples covering the polygon area. `Err(String)` — if triangulation fails (e.g. self-intersecting or degenerate input).

---

### `fn is_convex`  · [line 73](src/math/polygon.rs#L73)

Check if a polygon is convex.

Uses cross-product sign consistency at each vertex to determine convexity.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn is_convex(polygon: &[Vec2]) -> bool
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `polygon` | slice of `Vec2` vertices |

**Returns:** `true` if the polygon is convex; `false` if concave, self-intersecting, or fewer than 3 vertices.

---

### `fn field_of_view`  · [line 92](src/math/raycasting.rs#L92)

Computes a visibility polygon by casting rays at segment endpoints.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn field_of_view(ox: f32, oy: f32, segments: &[Segment], radius: f32) -> Vec<f32>
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `ox` | `f32`. |
| `oy` | `f32`. |
| `segments` | `&[Segment]`. |
| `radius` | `f32`. |

**Returns:** `Vec<f32>`. Casts rays towards each segment endpoint (plus small angular offsets) within `radius`, sorts the hit points by angle, and returns a flat polygon `[x0, y0, x1, y1, ...]`.

## Module: `math::spatial_hash` {#math-spatial-hash}

*Source: `src/math/spatial_hash.rs`*

Spatial hash for efficient broad-phase AABB collision queries.

Items are keyed by a string ID and stored with axis-aligned bounding boxes.
The grid partitions space into fixed-size cells for O(1) bucket lookup.

---

### `struct SpatialItem`  · [line 17](src/math/spatial_hash.rs#L17)

Entry in the spatial hash.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct SpatialItem
```

**Fields:**

|-------|-------------|
| `id` | `String`. |
| `x` | `f32`. |
| `y` | `f32`. |
| `w` | `f32`. |
| `h` | `f32`. |

---

### `struct SpatialHash`  · [line 35](src/math/spatial_hash.rs#L35)

Spatial hash for AABB queries.

Divides the 2D plane into a uniform grid of square cells. Each item is inserted into every cell its bounding box overlaps, enabling fast broad-phase collision queries.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct SpatialHash
```

**Fields:**

| Field | Type | Description |
|-------|------|-------------|
| `cell_size` | | *(private)* |
| `items` | | *(private)* |
| `buckets` | | *(private)* |

|-----------|-------------|
| `cell_size` | Side length of each grid cell. Larger values mean fewer |

**Returns:** `Vec<String>`. segment from `(x1, y1)` to `(x2, y2)`. Traverses cells along the segment and performs AABB–segment overlap tests on each candidate.

## Module: `math::srgb` {#math-srgb}

*Source: `src/math/srgb.rs`*

sRGB gamma ↔ linear color space conversion.

Implements the standard IEC 61966-2-1 (sRGB) transfer functions for
converting between gamma-encoded sRGB and linear light values.

---

| Parameter | Description |

**Returns:** `Vec<&ModInfo>`. When a custom load order is set via [`set_load_order`], it is respected: mods listed there appear first (in that order), followed by any remaining mods sorted by priority. Mods not registered are silently skipped.

---

### `fn ModManager::scan_folder`  · [line 268](src/modding/mod_manager.rs#L268)

Scan a directory for mods and register them.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn scan_folder(&mut self, path: &str) -> Vec<ModInfo>
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `path` | `&str`. |

**Returns:** `Vec<ModInfo>`. Each immediate subdirectory of `path` that contains a `mod.toml` file is parsed into a [`ModInfo`] and registered. Subdirectories without `mod.toml` are silently skipped. Expected `mod.toml` fields (all optional except `id`): ```toml id          = "my-mod" name        = "My Mod" version     = "1.2.0" author      = "Author Name" description = "What this mod does" priority    = 10 dependencies = ["other-mod"] ``` Returns the list of `ModInfo` objects that were discovered and registered. Returns an empty list if `path` does not exist or cannot be read.

---

## Module: `particle` {#particle}

*Source: `src/particle/mod.rs`*

Particle system module providing emitter-based 2D particle effects.

A `ParticleSystem` spawns short-lived `Particle` entities each frame,
advancing their position, velocity, and lifetime. Dead particles are
recycled, keeping allocation bounded by `ParticleConfig::max_particles`.

Supports multi-stop size/color/alpha interpolation, emission shapes,
radial/tangential acceleration, linear damping, relative mode, and texture-based rendering.

---

### `mod system`  · [line 10](src/particle/mod.rs#L10)

*No documentation.*

---


## Module: `particle::system` {#particle-system}

*Source: `src/particle/system.rs`*

Particle system module providing emitter-based 2D particle effects.

A `ParticleSystem` spawns short-lived `Particle` entities each frame,
advancing their position, velocity, and lifetime. Dead particles are
recycled, keeping allocation bounded by `ParticleConfig::max_particles`.

Supports multi-stop size/color/alpha interpolation, emission shapes,
radial/tangential acceleration, linear damping, relative mode, and texture-based rendering.

### `fn ParticleSystem::draw_commands`  · [line 786](src/particle/system.rs#L786)

Generates `DrawCommand`s for rendering all live particles.

```rust
pub fn draw_commands(&self, ox: f32, oy: f32) -> Vec<DrawCommand>
```

**Returns:** `Vec<DrawCommand>`. Each particle is drawn as a filled rectangle (untextured) or a textured sprite, sized and colored by multi-stop interpolation based on remaining lifetime. When `alpha_keyframes` are set, the alpha channel is overridden independently. When `relative_mode` is `Attached`, particle positions are offset by the emitter position.

| `oy` | World Y offset added to each particle position. |

### `fn interpolate_sizes`  · [line 906](src/particle/system.rs#L906)

Interpolate a multi-stop size array at normalised time `t` (0 = birth, 1 = death).

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn interpolate_sizes(sizes: &[f32], t: f32, variation: f32) -> f32
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `sizes` | `&[f32]`. |
| `t` | `f32`. |
| `variation` | `f32`. |

**Returns:** `f32`. The `variation` factor (0..1) scales down the interpolated size. With `variation = 0`, the full interpolated size is returned.

**Edge cases:**

- Empty `sizes`: returns `1.0`.
- Single value: returns `sizes[0] * (1 - variation)`.
- `t` is clamped to `[0, 1]`.

---

### `fn interpolate_colors`  · [line 935](src/particle/system.rs#L935)

Interpolate a multi-stop color array at normalised time `t` (0 = birth, 1 = death).


| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `colors` | `&[[f32; 4]]`. |
| `t` | `f32`. |

**Returns:** `[f32; 4]`.

**Edge cases:**

- Empty `colors`: returns white `[1, 1, 1, 1]`.
- Single value: returns that color.
- `t` is clamped to `[0, 1]`.

---

## Module: `pathfinding::astar` {#pathfinding-astar}

*Source: `src/pathfinding/astar.rs`*

A★ search with octile/Manhattan heuristic and Theta★ path smoothing.

---

### `fn astar`  · [line 73](src/pathfinding/astar.rs#L73)

Run A★ search on `grid` from `start` to `goal`.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn astar( grid: &NavGrid, start: (u32, u32), goal: (u32, u32), unit_size: u32, max_nodes: u32, ) -> (Option<Vec<(u32, u32)>>, bool)
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `grid` | `&NavGrid`. |
| `start` | `(u32, u32)`. |
| `goal` | `(u32, u32)`. |
| `unit_size` | `u32`. |
| `max_nodes` | `u32`. |

**Returns:** `(Option<Vec<(u32, u32)>>, bool)`. - `unit_size`: NxN footprint (1 for single-cell units). - `max_nodes`: upper bound on nodes expanded; 0 = unlimited. Returns `(path, complete)` where `path` is `Some(vec)` with the path from start to goal (or nearest reachable node) and `complete` indicates whether the goal was actually reached.

## Module: `pathfinding::async_pool` {#pathfinding-async-pool}

*Source: `src/pathfinding/async_pool.rs`*

Thread pool for asynchronous path computation.

Pathfinding requests are submitted with an ID and processed on worker
threads. Results are collected via non-blocking [`PathThreadPool::poll`].

---

## Module: `pathfinding::hpa` {#pathfinding-hpa}

*Source: `src/pathfinding/hpa.rs`*

Hierarchical Pathfinding A★ (HPA★) for fast long-range queries.

Divides the grid into chunks, finds boundary entrances, builds an abstract
graph, and searches at the chunk level before refining to tile-level paths.

---

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `grid` | `&NavGrid`. |
| `chunk_size` | `u32`. |

**Returns:** `AbstractGraph`. Divides the grid into `chunk_size × chunk_size` regions, finds entrance pairs on every inter-chunk boundary, and connects entrances within the same chunk via local A★.

### `struct NavGrid`  · [line 46](src/pathfinding/nav_grid.rs#L46)

A 2D grid of traversal costs used by pathfinding algorithms.

Cells are addressed with 0-based `(x, y)` coordinates in row-major order. A cost of `0` marks a cell as blocked; values `1..=255` represent movement cost.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct NavGrid
```

**Fields:**

| Field | Type | Description |
|-------|------|-------------|
| `width` | | *(private)* |
| `height` | | *(private)* |
| `costs` | | *(private)* |
| `chunk_size` | | *(private)* |
| `diagonal_mode` | | *(private)* |
| `dirty_rects` | | *(private)* |

---


**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `width` | `u32`. |
| `height` | `u32`. |

**Returns:** `Self`.

| `width` | `u32`. |
| `height` | `u32`. |
| `costs` | `Vec<u8>`. |

**Returns:** `Self`. `costs` must have exactly `width * height` elements. A cost of 0 marks blocked; 1-255 is traversal cost.

### `fn UnitPathfinder::heuristic_distance`  · [line 319](src/pathfinding/unit_pathfinder.rs#L319)

Octile heuristic distance between two points.

**Signature:**

## Module: `physics::body` {#physics-body}

### `enum BodyType`  · [line 11](src/physics/body.rs#L11)

Determines whether a physics body is affected by forces and gravity.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub enum BodyType
```

**Variants:**

| Variant | Description |
|---------|-------------|
| `Static` | Immovable body; does not respond to gravity or impulses. Used for terrain. |
| `Dynamic` | Movable body; subject to gravity, forces, and velocity integration. |
| `Sensor` | Trigger volume; detects overlaps but does not resolve collisions. |
