### `struct Body`  · [line 57](src/physics/body.rs#L57)

A rigid body with position, velocity, mass, shape, and restitution.

Bodies live in a `World` and are identified by their index. Use `World::get_body_mut` to access and modify them each frame.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct Body
```

**Fields:**

| Field | Description |
|-------|-------------|
| `position` | World-space centre position. |
| `velocity` | Linear velocity in world units per second. |
| `mass` | Mass in kg. |
| `body_type` | Static, Dynamic, Kinematic, or Sensor. |
| `shape` | Collision geometry (Rect or Circle). |
| `restitution` | Bounciness coefficient. |
| `friction` | Friction coefficient. |
| `angle` | Angular orientation in radians. |
| `angular_velocity` | Spin rate in radians/s. |
| `shape_ext` | Extended shape override (polygon, edge, chain). |

---

## Module: `physics` {#physics}

*Source: `src/physics/mod.rs`*

Physics simulation module backed by rapier2d.

Provides rigid-body simulation with circles, rectangles, sensors,
raycasting, joints, and collision event recording.

```rust
pub enum Shape
```

| `Circle` | Circle with a radius. |

| `Chain` | Connected chain of edges, optionally closed. |

## Module: `physics::world` {#physics-world}

*Source: `src/physics/world.rs`*

Rapier2d-backed physics world with backward-compatible Luna2D API.

Wraps the rapier2d simulation pipeline while exposing the same `Body`-based
interface. The `Body` struct is a sync buffer: mutations via `get_body_mut()`
are flushed into rapier on the next `step()` call, and rapier's computed
positions/velocities are read back after each step.

---

### `struct BodyContact`  · [line 70](src/physics/world.rs#L70)

Collision event generated by `World::step` when two bodies start overlapping.

Contains stable integer body IDs for the two bodies involved.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct BodyContact
```

**Fields:**

| Field | Description |
|-------|-------------|
| `body_a` | Index of the first body. |
| `body_b` | Index of the second body. |

---

### `fn World::step`  · [line 634](src/physics/world.rs#L634)

Advances the simulation by `dt` seconds.

1. Rebuild rapier colliders for bodies with changed shape/properties. 2. Push all body positions/velocities into rapier. 3. Step the rapier pipeline. 4. Read back positions/velocities for Dynamic bodies. 5. Record collision events.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn step(&mut self, dt: f32)
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `dt` | Time step in seconds. |

---

## Module: `quest` {#quest}

*Source: `src/quest/mod.rs`*

Quest and objective tracking system for Luna2D games.

Provides `Quest`, `Objective`, `QuestStage`, `JournalEntry`, and `QuestLog`
for building RPG-style quest systems with stages, conditions, and journal notes.

---

### `enum QuestStatus`  · [line 14](src/quest/mod.rs#L14)

Lifecycle state of a quest.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub enum QuestStatus
```

**Variants:**

| Variant | Description |
|---------|-------------|
| `Available` | Quest is available but not yet accepted. |
| `Active` | Quest has been accepted and is in progress. |
| `Completed` | All required objectives are complete. |
| `Failed` | Quest was abandoned or failed. |

---

### `enum ObjectiveStatus`  · [line 54](src/quest/mod.rs#L54)

Lifecycle state of a single objective.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub enum ObjectiveStatus
```

**Variants:**

| Variant | Description |
|---------|-------------|
| `Pending` | Not yet started. |
| `Active` | In progress. |
| `Done` | Successfully completed. |
| `Skipped` | Skipped (optional objectives can be skipped). |
| `Failed` | Failed. |

### `struct Objective`  · [line 100](src/quest/mod.rs#L100)

A single trackable task within a quest.

Supports count-based progress (`current`/`required`) and optional tagging.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct Objective
```

**Fields:**

| Field | Type | Description |
|-------|------|-------------|
| `id` | `String` | Unique identifier within the parent quest. |
| `description` | `String` | Human-readable display text. |
| `current` | `u32` | Current progress count. |
| `required` | `u32` | Required count to mark as done. |
| `mandatory` | `bool` | Whether this objective must be completed (true = required, false = optional). |
| `status` | `ObjectiveStatus` | Current lifecycle status. |
| `tags` | `Vec<String>` | Arbitrary tags for filtering (e.g., `"kill"`, `"collect"`, `"talk"`). |
| `visible` | `bool` | Whether the objective is shown to the player. |

---


### `struct JournalEntry`  · [line 235](src/quest/mod.rs#L235)

```rust
pub struct JournalEntry
```

**Fields:**

| `index` | `u32` | Monotone sequence number (assigned by `Quest`). |
| `text` | `String` | Text body of the entry. |

### `struct Quest`  · [line 253](src/quest/mod.rs#L253)

A quest with stages, objectives, and a journal.

Stages are ordered; the quest advances through them as the game logic calls `next_stage()` or `goto_stage()`.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct Quest
```

**Fields:**

| Field | Type | Description |
|-------|------|-------------|
| `id` | `String` | Unique identifier. |
| `title` | `String` | Display title. |
| `description` | `String` | Multi-line description shown to the player. |
| `status` | `QuestStatus` | Current lifecycle status. |
| `stages` | `Vec<QuestStage>` | Ordered stage list. |
| `current_stage` | `usize` | Index into `stages` of the active stage (0-based). |
| `journal` | `Vec<JournalEntry>` | Journal entries (append-only). |
| `metadata` | `HashMap<String, String>` | Arbitrary key-value string metadata (e.g., `giver`, `location`, `category`). |
| `visible` | `bool` | Whether the quest is visible in the quest log. |
| `reward` | `String` | Reward description (informational only; fulfilment is game-side). |
| `journal_counter` | | *(private)* |

---

### `struct QuestLog`  · [line 413](src/quest/mod.rs#L413)

Registry of all quests for a game session.

## Module: `resource` {#resource}

*Source: `src/resource/mod.rs`*

Resource economy system: named resources with capacity, flow rates, decay,
interest, upkeep, overflow policies, reservations, and conversions.

Designed for RTS, management, survival, and RPG economy patterns where
the game tracks multiple named numeric values (gold, wood, mana, food)
that change over time with configurable rates.

---

### `enum OverflowPolicy`  · [line 12](src/resource/mod.rs#L12)

Policy governing what happens when adding exceeds capacity.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub enum OverflowPolicy
```

**Variants:**

| Variant | Description |
|---------|-------------|
| `Clamp` | Excess is lost; value is clamped to capacity (default). |
| `Lose` | The entire addition is rejected if it would exceed capacity. |
| `Wrap` | Value wraps around from minimum. |

---

### `fn OverflowPolicy::as_str`  · [line 23](src/resource/mod.rs#L23)

Returns the string name of this policy.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn as_str(&self) -> &'static str
```

---

### `fn OverflowPolicy::from_str`  · [line 32](src/resource/mod.rs#L32)

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn from_str(s: &str) -> Self
```

### `struct SaveManager`  · [line 31](src/savegame/save_data.rs#L31)

Pure-data save manager providing registration of named collectors, schema versioning, dirty-state tracking, and auto-save timer.

Actual serialisation and filesystem calls happen on the Lua side; this struct tracks the bookkeeping.


| Parameter | Description |

| `depth` | `u32`. |

**Returns:** `Result<String, String>`. Supports nil, bool, number (f64), string, and nested tables (HashMap). Does not handle userdata, functions, or circular references.

## Module: `scene` {#scene}

*Source: `src/scene/mod.rs`*

Scene stack module for managing game scene lifecycle, transitions, and depth-sorted rendering.

Provides a LIFO stack of Lua scene tables with lifecycle callbacks (`enter`, `leave`,
`pause`, `resume`, `update`, `draw`), animated transitions (fade, slide), a named
scene registry, inter-scene data passing, and a `DepthSorter` for z-ordered draw batching.

---

### `mod depth_sorter`  · [line 8](src/scene/mod.rs#L8)

depth_sorter.

---

### `mod stack`  · [line 10](src/scene/mod.rs#L10)

stack.

---

### `mod transition`  · [line 12](src/scene/mod.rs#L12)

transition.

---

### `struct SceneStack`  · [line 14](src/scene/stack.rs#L14)

The scene stack manages a LIFO stack of scene references.

Scenes are identified by `SceneId` values. The Lua API layer maps these to `mlua::RegistryKey` references for actual Lua table access.

### `fn SceneStack::pop`  · [line 88](src/scene/stack.rs#L88)

| `transition_type` | `TransitionType`. |
| `duration` | `f32`. |

**Returns:** `Result<(SceneId, Option<SceneId>), String>`. Returns `(popped_id, revealed_id)` — the removed scene and the newly exposed top. Returns `Err` if the stack is empty.

---

### `fn SceneStack::switch_to`  · [line 116](src/scene/stack.rs#L116)

Replace the top scene with a new one.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn switch_to( &mut self, scene_id: SceneId, transition_type: TransitionType, duration: f32, ) -> Option<SceneId>
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `scene_id` | `SceneId`. |
| `transition_type` | `TransitionType`. |
| `duration` | `f32`. |

**Returns:** `Option<SceneId>`. Returns the old top scene ID so the caller can invoke `leave()` on it. If the stack is empty, just pushes the new scene.

---

## Module: `stats` {#stats}

*Source: `src/stats/mod.rs`*

RPG character sheet and stat system.

Provides a flexible attribute system with buffs, derived stats, traits,
skills, perks, XP/levelling, action points, morale, and resistances.

---

### `enum StackMode`  · [line 10](src/stats/mod.rs#L10)

How a buff stacks with existing buffs of the same name.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub enum StackMode
```

**Variants:**

| Variant | Description |
|---------|-------------|
| `None` | Reapplying the effect resets its duration. |
| `Duration` | Reapplying extends the remaining duration. |
| `Intensity` | Reapplying adds a stack count (up to max_stacks). |

---

### `struct Buff`  · [line 21](src/stats/mod.rs#L21)

A single stat modifier attached to an attribute.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct Buff
```

**Fields:**

| Field | Type | Description |
|-------|------|-------------|
| `stat` | `String` | Which attribute this buff modifies. |
| `add` | `f64` | Additive bonus (added before multiply). |
| `mul` | `f64` | Multiplicative factor (default 1.0). |
| `duration` | `f64` | Seconds until expiry. -1 = permanent. |
| `source` | `String` | Descriptive source string. |
| `remaining` | `f64` | Remaining time in seconds. |

## Module: `thread::channel` {#thread-channel}

*Source: `src/thread/channel.rs`*

Thread-safe channel for Lua inter-thread communication.

Provides an MPMC (multi-producer, multi-consumer) queue that can be
shared between the main game thread and background Lua threads via
`Arc<Channel>`. Only primitive Lua values (nil, bool, number, string)
can cross thread boundaries.

---

### `enum ChannelValue`  · [line 26](src/thread/channel.rs#L26)

Serializable values that can be sent between threads.

**Signature:**
```rust

```

**Variants:**

| Variant | Description |
|---------|-------------|
| `Nil` | Nil variant. |
| `Bool` | Bool variant. |
| `Number` | Number variant. |
| `String` | String variant. |

---

### `struct Channel`  · [line 42](src/thread/channel.rs#L42)

Thread-safe MPMC channel for Lua inter-thread communication.

Internally uses a `Mutex<VecDeque>` protected queue with a `Condvar` for blocking `demand()` calls. Safe to wrap in `Arc` and share across OS threads.

## Module: `thread::worker` {#thread-worker}

*Source: `src/thread/worker.rs`*

Background Lua thread with independent VM.

Each `LuaThread` spawns an OS thread running its own `mlua::Lua` instance.
Communication with the main thread happens exclusively through `Channel`
objects — no Lua state is shared across threads.

---

## Module: `tilemap::autotile_sheet` {#tilemap-autotile-sheet}

*Source: `src/tilemap/autotile_sheet.rs`*

AutoTileSheet — loads a pre-arranged autotile image and generates TileSet tiles + bitmask rules.

## 48-tile quarter-tile format

For high-quality composite autotile rendering, [`AutoTileSheet`] supports a 48-tile
sub-tile format where each full tile is assembled from **four quarter-tile pieces** (TL, TR,
BL, BR).  The source image must be **`3*tile_w` × `4*tile_h` pixels** — a 6-column ×
8-row grid of `(tile_w/2 × tile_h/2)` quarter pieces.

Call [`AutoTileSheet::get_quarter_rects`] with the raw 8-bit neighbour bitmask to obtain the
four [`Rect`]s to blit.  Use [`AutoTileSheet::get_composite48_grid_quad`] when the source atlas
stores the 48 pre-composed tile variants in a 6 × 8 full-tile grid instead.

### Bitmask bit layout (raw 8-bit)

```text
bit 0 = N   bit 4 = NE
bit 1 = E   bit 5 = SE
bit 2 = S   bit 6 = SW
bit 3 = W   bit 7 = NW
```

---

### `enum AutoTileLayout`  · [line 36](src/tilemap/autotile_sheet.rs#L36)

Predefined autotile sheet layout variants.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub enum AutoTileLayout
```

**Variants:**

| Variant | Description |
|---------|-------------|
| `Blob47` | Blob47 variant. |
| `Composite48` | 48-tile composite variant. |
| `Minimal16` | Minimal16 variant. |

---

### `struct AutoTileSheet`  · [line 50](src/tilemap/autotile_sheet.rs#L50)

### `fn AutoTileSheet::get_grid_quad`  · [line 328](src/tilemap/autotile_sheet.rs#L328)

**Signature:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|

| `cols` | `u32`. |

**Returns:** `Rect`. Unlike [`Self::get_quad`] (single row), this method assumes the tiles are arranged in a grid with `cols` columns, matching the pre-composed 48-tile 6-column × 8-row layout (`cols = 6`). Returns a zero-size rect if `index >= tile_count`.

---

### `fn AutoTileSheet::get_quarter_rects`  · [line 386](src/tilemap/autotile_sheet.rs#L386)

Returns the four quarter-tile source [`Rect`]s for the given raw 8-bit neighbour bitmask.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn get_quarter_rects(&self, bitmask: u16) -> [Rect; 4]
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `bitmask` | `u16`. |

**Returns:** `[Rect; 4]`. The output array is `[TL, TR, BL, BR]`. Each rect addresses a `(tile_w/2 × tile_h/2)` area inside a **48-tile composite source image**, which must be exactly `3*tile_w × 4*tile_h` pixels in size. ## Source image layout (6 q-columns × 8 q-rows) | qcol | 0 | 1 | 2 | 3 | 4 | 5 | |---|---|---|---|---|---|---| | **qrow 0** | IC-TL | IC-TR | N-edge TL | N-edge TR | Ctr-TL | (unused) | | **qrow 1** | IC-BL | IC-BR | S-edge BL | S-edge BR | Ctr-BL | (unused) | | **qrow 2** | (unused) | (unused) | (unused) | (unused) | Ctr-TL(f) | Ctr-TR(f) | | **qrow 3** | (unused) | (unused) | (unused) | (unused) | Ctr-BL(f) | Ctr-BR(f) | | **qrow 4** | W-edge TL | E-edge TR | (unused) | (unused) | (unused) | (unused) | | **qrow 5** | W-edge BL | E-edge BR | (unused) | (unused) | (unused) | (unused) | | **qrow 6** | OC-TL | OC-TR | (unused) | (unused) | (unused) | (unused) | | **qrow 7** | OC-BL | OC-BR | (unused) | (unused) | (unused) | (unused) | **IC** = inner corner (N+W present but NW absent), **Ctr** = center (all present), **N/S/W/E-edge** = one side open, **OC** = outer corner (two adjacent sides open). ## Bitmask bits `bit0=N, bit1=E, bit2=S, bit3=W, bit4=NE, bit5=SE, bit6=SW, bit7=NW`

---

### `fn AutoTileSheet::get_quarter_dst_rects`  · [line 414](src/tilemap/autotile_sheet.rs#L414)

Returns the four **destination** sub-rects within a tile at world position `(x, y)`.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn get_quarter_dst_rects(&self, x: f32, y: f32) -> [Rect; 4]
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `x` | `f32`. |
| `y` | `f32`. |

**Returns:** `[Rect; 4]`. The output array is `[TL, TR, BL, BR]`. Useful for rendering composite quarter tiles using four small blit calls instead of one full-tile blit.

---


## Module: `tilemap::chunk` {#tilemap-chunk}

*Source: `src/tilemap/chunk.rs`*

Chunk-based tilemap storage for large and infinite maps.

[`ChunkMap`] stores tiles in fixed-size square chunks using a [`HashMap`].
Only chunks that have been written to are allocated, allowing sparse, large,
or infinite maps without up-front memory commitment.

Tile coordinates use `i32` to support negative positions (e.g., a map centred
at the origin where negative X/Y are valid map space).

---

### `struct ChunkMap`  · [line 20](src/tilemap/chunk.rs#L20)

A chunk-based tilemap that supports large and infinite maps through sparse storage.

Tiles are stored in square chunks of `chunk_size × chunk_size` tiles.  Chunks are allocated on first write and can be individually unloaded to reclaim memory. Reads from unloaded chunks return [`ChunkMap::DEFAULT_GID`] (0).

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct ChunkMap
```

**Fields:**

| Field | Type | Description |
|-------|------|-------------|
| `chunk_size` | | *(private)* |
| `chunks` | | *(private)* |

---

### `const ChunkMap::DEFAULT_GID`  · [line 27](src/tilemap/chunk.rs#L27)

### `fn to_screen_iso`  · [line 24](src/tilemap/coords.rs#L24)

Converts tile coordinates to screen position using diamond isometric projection.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn to_screen_iso(tx: f32, ty: f32, tile_w: f32, tile_h: f32) -> Vec2
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `tx` | `f32`. |
| `ty` | `f32`. |
| `tile_w` | `f32`. |
| `tile_h` | `f32`. |

**Returns:** `Vec2`. - `screen.x = (tx - ty) * tile_w / 2` - `screen.y = (tx + ty) * tile_h / 2`

## Module: `tilemap::isomap` {#tilemap-isomap}

*Source: `src/tilemap/isomap.rs`*

Multi-level isometric tilemap for OpenXcom-style rendering.

Each map cell holds four tile parts rendered in painter's algorithm order:
`Floor`, `NorthWall`, `WestWall`, `Object`. Z-levels stack vertically with
a configurable pixel offset so higher floors appear above lower ones.

---

### `enum IsoTilePart`  · [line 22](src/tilemap/isomap.rs#L22)

The four sub-slots within each isometric map cell, rendered in this order.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub enum IsoTilePart
```

**Variants:**

| Variant | Description |
|---------|-------------|
| `Floor` | Floor variant. |
| `NorthWall` | NorthWall variant. |
| `WestWall` | WestWall variant. |
| `Object` | Object variant. |

---

| `tile_y` | `u32`. |

| `screen_y` | `f32`. |

---

### `struct IsoMap`  · [line 217](src/tilemap/isomap.rs#L217)

Multi-level isometric tilemap with painter's-algorithm draw iteration.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct IsoMap
```

**Fields:**

| Field | Description |
|-------|-------------|
| `width` | `u32`. |
| `height` | `u32`. |
| `tile_w` | `u32`. |
| `tile_h` | `u32`. |
| `level_height` | `u32`. |
| `origin_x` | `f32`. |
| `origin_y` | `f32`. |

**Coordinate system:**

```text
screen_x = origin_x + (tx - ty) * tile_w / 2
screen_y = origin_y + (tx + ty) * tile_h / 2 - tz * level_height
```

**Draw order:**

[`draw_iter`](IsoMap::draw_iter) yields items in the correct painter's
algorithm order for a standard isometric view with the camera positioned at
the top-left corner:

1. Diagonal `d = tx + ty` increases from `0` to `(W-1) + (H-1)`.
2. For each diagonal, tiles iterate in ascending `tx` order.
3. For each tile, Z-levels iterate from bottom (`0`) to `active_z`.
4. For each Z-level, parts iterate Floor → NorthWall → WestWall → Object.

---

### `fn IsoMap::new`  · [line 249](src/tilemap/isomap.rs#L249)

**Signature:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|

| `height` | `u32`. |
| `tile_w` | `u32`. |
| `tile_h` | `u32`. |
| `level_height` | `u32`. |

**Returns:** `Self`. Add levels with [`add_level`](Self::add_level) before placing tiles.

---

### `fn IsoMap::draw_iter`  · [line 456](src/tilemap/isomap.rs#L456)

Returns all draw items in painter's algorithm order for rendering up to

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn draw_iter(&self, active_z: usize) -> Vec<IsoDrawItem>
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `active_z` | `usize`. |

**Returns:** `Vec<IsoDrawItem>`. and including level `active_z`. If `active_z` >= the number of levels, it is clamped to the last level. **Every** tile part is yielded, including those with `gid == 0`. Lua can skip drawing when `gid == 0` to keep the Rust side simple.

**Order:**

For each diagonal `d` (0 … W+H-2), for each `(tx, ty)` in that diagonal
with ascending `tx`, for each `z` in `0..=active_z` (if the level is
visible), for each part in Floor, NorthWall, WestWall, Object order.

---

### `fn MapGen::generate`  · [line 824](src/tilemap/mapgen.rs#L824)

Generates a [`TileMap`] from a [`MapGroup`] using an optional script and seed.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn generate( &mut self, group: &MapGroup, script_index: Option<usize>, seed: Option<u64>, ) -> TileMap
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `group` | `&MapGroup`. |
| `script_index` | `Option<usize>`. |
| `seed` | `Option<u64>`. |

**Returns:** `TileMap`. The map width = `grid_w * segment_size`, height = `grid_h * segment_size`. Creates one layer and applies script steps. Currently implements: - [`StepType::FillRandom`]: fills tiles with random GIDs from available blocks. - [`StepType::PlaceBlock`]: stamps a specific block's tiles into the map. - [`StepType::FillRect`]: fills a rectangle with `tile_id`. - Other step types: no-op (stub).

---

## Module: `tilemap` {#tilemap}

Tilemap engine module — TileSet, TileMap, AutoTileSheet, IsoMap, ChunkMap, TMX loader, and procedural generation types.

Auto-tile atlas with bitmask-based tile selection.

Sparse chunk-based tilemap storage for large and infinite maps.

Coordinate helpers for tile ↔ world conversions.

### `mod isomap`  · [line 10](src/tilemap/mod.rs#L10)

Multi-level isometric tilemap with painter's-algorithm draw order.

### `mod mapgen`  · [line 12](src/tilemap/mod.rs#L12)

Procedural map generation scripts and room placement.

### `mod tilemap`  · [line 15](src/tilemap/mod.rs#L15)

Core tilemap: layers, tile CRUD, sweep queries, and serialization.

### `mod tileset`  · [line 17](src/tilemap/mod.rs#L17)

```rust
pub fn angle(self) -> f32
```

**Returns:** `f32`. This uses standard math angles where east=0 and angles increase counter-clockwise, but in screen space (Y-down) east=0 and south=PI/2.

### `struct TileWalker`  · [line 134](src/tilemap/tile_walker.rs#L134)

Tile-based movement controller for first-person grid navigation.

## Module: `tilemap::tmx` {#tilemap-tmx}

*Source: `src/tilemap/tmx.rs`*

Tiled TMX map format loader.

Parses `.tmx` files produced by the [Tiled Map Editor](https://www.mapeditor.org/).
TMX is an XML-based format; this module uses [`roxmltree`] for parsing.

Supports:
- Orthogonal, isometric, staggered, and hexagonal map orientations.
- Tile data encoding: XML elements, CSV, and Base64 (with optional zlib/gzip compression).
- Inline and external tileset references (TSX source returned as a path string for caller resolution).
- Object layers and image layers (parsed to metadata; not converted to [`TileMap`] data).

Does NOT support:
- Infinite maps (chunk-based TMX format): treat as a warning; use [`ChunkMap`] directly.
- Embedded TSX tileset files — the caller must load them separately.

[`ChunkMap`]: super::chunk::ChunkMap

---

### `enum TmxOrientation`  · [line 31](src/tilemap/tmx.rs#L31)

**Variants:**

| Variant | Description |
|---------|-------------|

| `Staggered` | Staggered variant. |

### `fn load_tmx`  · [line 289](src/tilemap/tmx.rs#L289)

Parses a TMX file given its XML content as a string.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn load_tmx(xml: &str) -> Result<TmxMap, String>
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `xml` | `&str`. |

**Returns:** `Result<TmxMap, String>`. Returns a fully-populated [`TmxMap`], or an error string describing the problem. ### Tile data encoding - **XML**: `<tile gid="…"/>` child elements — always supported. - **CSV**: Comma-separated list of GIDs — supported without extra dependencies. - **Base64**: Base64-encoded little-endian `u32` array — supported via the `base64` crate. - **Base64 + zlib**: Further decompressed with `flate2` — supported. - **Base64 + gzip**: Gzip-decompressed with `flate2` — supported. - **Base64 + zstd**: Not supported (returns an error).

---

### `fn Clock::tick`  · [line 56](src/timer/clock.rs#L56)

Advances the clock by one frame, updating delta time, total time, and rolling FPS.

Call once per frame at the top of the game loop. The rolling FPS is updated every second using a frame-accumulation window.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn tick(&mut self) -> f64
```

**Returns:** `f64` — The elapsed time since the last `tick` call, in seconds.

### `fn Clock::fps`  · [line 102](src/timer/clock.rs#L102)

Returns the rolling frames-per-second measurement.

Updated once per second. Returns `0.0` during the first second of execution.

**Signature:**

### `fn Clock::average_delta`  · [line 120](src/timer/clock.rs#L120)

Returns the average delta time over the last N frames (up to 60).

Returns `0.0` if no frames have been ticked yet. Once the buffer is full, averages over the entire 60-frame window.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub fn average_delta(&self) -> f64
```

**Returns:** `f64` — Rolling average delta in seconds.

## Module: `timer::scheduler` {#timer-scheduler}

*Source: `src/timer/scheduler.rs`*

Scheduled event manager for delayed and repeating timed callbacks.

Provides [`Scheduler`] for one-shot delays, repeating timers, named events,
individual pause/resume, global time-scale, and on-the-fly interval changes.

## Usage
```rust,no_run
# use luna2d::timer::Scheduler;
let mut sched = Scheduler::new();
let id = sched.after(2.0);          // fires once after 2 seconds
let rid = sched.every(0.5, -1);     // fires every 0.5 s indefinitely
sched.set_time_scale(0.5);          // run at half speed
let fired = sched.update(0.1);      // advance; returns IDs that fired
sched.cancel(rid);
```

---

### `struct Scheduler`  · [line 55](src/timer/scheduler.rs#L55)

Manages a collection of timed events (one-shot and repeating).

Each event has an integer ID (returned on creation) that can be used for cancellation, pause/resume, and property reads. Named events can also be cancelled by their string name.

**Signature:**
```rust
pub struct Scheduler
```

**Fields:**

| Field | Type | Description |
|-------|------|-------------|
| `events` | | *(private)* |
| `next_id` | | *(private)* |
| `time_scale` | | *(private)* |
